International Commercial Telegrams

丨Special Commercial Report by Reuters, August 10th丨

Gold and Silver

London Gold Price: The London gold price remained unchanged today at 138 shillings and 1 penny.

London Silver Bars: In the London silver market, China sold a large number of futures contracts, but speculators bought them. The United States purchased spot goods. The spot price was 21 pence and 4375, the same as yesterday's price. Futures were 21 pence and 375, down 0.0625.

New York Silver Bars: The forward silver price in New York was closed today.

Bombay Silver Bars: The Bombay silver market was stable today following news from the United States. The spot price was 59 rupees and 11 annas, the August price was 59 rupees and 12 annas, and the September price was 59 rupees and 14 annas, all up 6 pounds each.

Exchange Rates

British-American: This morning, after a slight covering by those short on US dollars in the foreign exchange market, selling continued. The US-British exchange rate opened at 5.0925 yuan, 25 points lower than the closing US-British exchange rate yesterday. At 10:10 AM, the price fell to 5.0825 yuan, and at 11:00 AM it rose by 625 to 5.08875 yuan. At noon, it continued to rise to 5.0925 yuan. The upward trend continued in the afternoon, and at 2:00 PM the price was 5.095 yuan. Also, one US dollar was equivalent to three shillings, eleven pence and one zero five British gold.

British-French: The opening price was 6 pounds higher than yesterday's closing price, at 76.34 francs. At 11:00 AM, it fell by 6 pounds, the same as yesterday's closing price, but this drop was quickly reversed. At 2:00 PM, the price was 76.34 francs, the same as today's opening price.

US-British: In the New York foreign exchange market, the British pound was slightly firm today. The US-British exchange rate opened 25 points higher at 5.095 yuan. The upward trend continued in the morning, and the latest price was 5.0975 yuan.

Securities

New York: Before the opening of the New York Stock Exchange, factors favorable to the market were: (1) President Roosevelt announced that he did not want to harm honest businesses, and (2) commodity market conditions remained strong. Factors unfavorable to the market were: (1) the US dollar weakened due to the news of silver nationalization, and (2) the autumn business climate was still uncertain. At the opening of the New York Stock Exchange, profit-taking was triggered by yesterday's gains, but price fluctuations were generally small. Investor sentiment was still stable, and the market was not expected to change significantly.

Cotton and Wheat

American Cotton: The New York cotton market opened 10 points lower than yesterday's closing price at 13.74 cents. The price continued to decline in the morning.

British Cotton: Liverpool cotton market prices continued to rise today. At 1:00 PM, the October price was 7.20, up 7 points from yesterday's closing price.

Indian Cotton: The Bombay cotton market also rose today due to buying by futures traders. Market conditions were firm. The April/May Belo cotton price was 237 rupees and 75, up 75 from yesterday.

American Wheat: Wheat market opening prices remained unchanged but tended to fall.

British Wheat: Liverpool wheat market prices rose today. At 1:00 PM, the October price was 6 shillings, 3 pence and 875, up 1 penny from yesterday's closing price.

Rubber

London: London rubber opened firmly today. The midday transaction price for October/December was 7 pence and 6875, up 125.

New York: Rubber opened unchanged in New York, but then fell by 17 points.

Facts: Chen Duxiu and Peng Shuzhi joined the Communist Party in 1920, and were appointed by the Third International as Standing Committee Members of the Chinese Communist Party, with Chen Duxiu concurrently serving as Secretary. They jointly executed the strategies instructed by the Third International, leading party members in activities in mainland China. Later, the party split into Stalinist and Trotskyist factions. Power was entirely controlled by the Stalinist faction. Chen Duxiu and Peng Shuzhi, because they were inclined towards the Trotskyist faction, were removed from their positions by the Third International in 1927, and expelled from the party in 1929. They then gathered comrades in Shanghai to secretly organize the Chinese Communist Party Left Opposition (hereinafter referred to as the CCP Opposition). Their goal was to unite workers, students, and peasants to organize a Soviet government and oppose the Stalinist faction's use of bandits and defeated soldiers to lead peasant uprisings in China. They compiled various writings, or issued various publications in the name of the CCP Opposition, and spread various leaflets in the name of resisting Japan, propagating the faction's doctrines in Shanghai, Tianjin, Hong Kong, and other places, hoping to overthrow the National Government and organize a Soviet government under the dictatorship of the proletariat. Wang Wu, Pu Yifan, and Wang Zhaoqun were all organizational members of the CCP Opposition, and Wang Wu and Pu Yifan were promoted to be alternate members of the Central Executive Committee of the faction. Guo Jinghao joined the CCP Opposition in 1929 and was responsible for organizational work and student movements. On October 15, 1932, Peng Shuzhi, Pu Yifan, Wang Wu, Wang Zhaoqun, and Xie Shaoshan were holding a regular weekly meeting at Xie Shaoshan's home, No. 210, Chunyang Lane, Dong Youheng Road, Shanghai. After the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau received a tip-off, it immediately sent personnel to Chunyang Lane with the police to arrest Peng Shuzhi and others on the spot. They then went to various places to arrest Chen Duxiu and Guo Jinghao, along with the propaganda documents and books they had seized, and transferred them to the Shanghai High Court Second Branch, which transferred them to the Jiangsu High Court Prosecutor for investigation and prosecution.

Reasons: In the investigation and in the original court, Chen Duxiu and Peng Shuzhi fully confessed how they joined the Communist Party, how they were appointed by the Third International as Standing Committee Members of the Chinese Communist Party, how they were removed from their positions and party membership by the Third International because they were inclined towards the Trotskyist faction, how they organized the Chinese Communist Party Left Opposition in Shanghai, and how they propagated their doctrines to workers, students, and other groups, hoping to overthrow the National Government and establish a Soviet regime under the dictatorship of the proletariat. What should be investigated is whether the faction has disturbed public order in addition to propaganda work, and whether it mutually supports the Stalinist faction in mainland China. Therefore, this court investigated Chen Duxiu's edited "Proletarian" and "Regarding the So-Called Red Army Problem," which stated that "The communist parties of dozens of countries around the world have always followed Engels's teachings and dare not adopt the policy of using vagrant proletarians (referring to bandits and defeated soldiers). Now the traitors of the Chinese workers' movement, Li Lisan, Xiang Zhongfa, Zhou Enlai, etc., (all of the Third International Stalinist faction) are using this kind of vagrant proletariat as guards and pillars, simply treating them as the main force of the proletarian revolutionary movement, attempting to expand and rely on the so-called Red Army based on the vagrant proletariat to lead peasants in guerrilla warfare. Except for being defeated, bought off, disintegrated by internal strife by the ruling class, or gradually compromising with the rural bourgeoisie and becoming their White Army, they cannot have other prospects." In the first volume, fourth issue of Spark, Peng Shuzhi's article "The Stalinists have an Estimate of the Manchurian Incident and the Crisis of the Anti-Japanese Movement" stated, "The Stalinist faction only trusts the Red Army, believing that with the Red Army, they can conquer the world. The armed struggle of peasants in Hunan, Hubei, and Jiangxi is a fact, but they neglect the urban workers' movement and place all their illusions and hopes on these armed peasants. This is the main reason why they have been stuck in a dead end for several years." Their attack on the Stalinist faction in China, that it should not use vagrants to lead peasant uprisings, is clearly expressed. Furthermore, Chen Duxiu confessed, "The Red Army should be purely organized by workers and peasants after the establishment of the Soviet government and should not be mixed with bandits. Moreover, there is no need for a Red Army now." Peng Shuzhi confessed, "We advocate that the Red Army should be purely organized by workers and peasants, and we do not advocate that there be bandits in the Red Army. We believe that there is no need for a Red Army now, and it is necessary to wait until the Soviet government is established before organizing a Red Army." It is clear that Chen Duxiu and Peng Shuzhi not only stand in opposition to the Stalinist faction in mainland China, but also that their method of activity, in addition to propaganda work, does not currently involve disturbing public order. This can also be confirmed. As for whether their propaganda writing reaches the level of treason, it is also a question that should be studied in this case. The publications edited by Chen Duxiu and Peng Shuzhi and issued in the name of the CCP Opposition are as many as over a hundred kinds, none of which do not contain writing that opposes the current state of the country and opposes the National Government. The most prominent publications, such as "Spark," "Campus Life," "Proletarian," "Hot Lake," and various leaflets distributed in the name of resisting Japan, as well as political resolutions issued in the name of the CCP Opposition, either state that the Outline of National Reconstruction is not applicable to China and should be torn up, or state that the National Government is organized by the bourgeoisie and should be overthrown. Peeking at their intentions, it is nothing more than wanting to completely destroy the current state of the country and reorganize a Soviet government under the dictatorship of the proletariat. Its ability to shake the foundations of the country is evident. According to the legislative intent of the Emergency Law for the Punishment of Acts Endangering the Republic, it cannot be said that it is not treason propaganda. Furthermore, the foundation of a nation is based on sovereignty, and the sovereignty of the Republic of China belongs to the people. All citizens of the Republic of China, without distinction of gender, race, religion, or class, are equal under the law. Articles 2 and 6 of the Provisional Constitution stipulate this. In contrast, the Soviet system only entrusts its sovereignty to the special class of peasants and workers, and cannot be compared to it. Chen Duxiu and others advocate that apart from changing from a democracy to an imperial system, which is treasonous, the organization of the Soviet regime has nothing to do with the essence of the founding of the Republic of China, which is particularly far-fetched. The original trial's finding that Chen Duxiu and Peng Shuzhi organized a group with the purpose of endangering the Republic and used writing to promote treason is correct. However, the original trial sentenced Chen Duxiu and Peng Shuzhi, who were inclined towards the Trotskyist faction and opposed the Stalinist faction's use of bandits and defeated soldiers to lead peasant armed uprisings, to thirteen years of imprisonment each, considering that they had no self-interest and were still scholars who were deeply thoughtful and painstaking, which is somewhat severe. Generally, Chen Duxiu and Peng Shuzhi's appeal argues that the original judgment was improper based on legal opinions, which is insufficient to be accepted, but their statement of disagreement is not without reason. Furthermore, Wang Wu only admitted that he had previously joined the Communist Party and had been sentenced to six years of imprisonment by the Shanghai Provisional Military Court, and that after being released on bail, he became an alternate member of the Central Standing Committee of the CCP Opposition and participated in regular weekly meetings, which he completely denied. Pu Yifan also admitted after being arrested that he had organized the Communist Party and served as an alternate member of the Central Standing Committee of the CCP Opposition. However, Wang Wu and Pu Yifan were at Xie Shaoshan's home, No. 210, Chunyang Lane, Dong Youheng Road, Shanghai, on October 15, 1932, holding a regular weekly meeting with Peng Shuzhi, Wang Zhaoqun, and Xie Shaoshan, and were arrested on the spot. This is an undeniable fact. Furthermore, Xie Shaoshan testified in the Shanghai Public Concession Police Department, "This place is often used as a meeting place. The Standing Committee includes five members: Chen Duxiu, Peng Shuzhi, Pu Yifan, Luo Shifan, and Song Fengchun (referring to Wang Wu). The last one had just been released from Caohejing Prison. This was the first time he had participated in the meeting. On the day I was arrested, they were holding a regular weekly meeting." When questioned by the judge of the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court, "What kind of organization is your place?" she replied, "My place is the Trotskyist leadership organization." When asked, "Where do you hold your meetings?" she replied, "We hold them every Saturday at my house." When asked, "What is Peng Shuzhi's position?" she replied, "He is a Standing Committee member." When asked, "What about Pu Yifan and Wang Wu?" she replied, "They are also Standing Committee members." When asked, "How many Standing Committee members are there?" she replied, "There are five in total, all of whom have been arrested. However, Chen Duxiu is the Chairman of the Standing Committee, Wang Wu only participated for the first time, and I am the Secretary of the Standing Committee." In addition, Peng Shuzhi also stated in the investigation that the alternate Standing Committee members were Pu Yifan and Song Fengchun. It is clear that Wang Wu and Pu Yifan are important members of the CCP Opposition and were arrested for participating in regular weekly meetings, which cannot be denied. However, Wang Wu and Pu Yifan have consistently insisted that they have nothing to do with the CCP Opposition and have not been promoted to the Standing Committee. Chen Duxiu and Peng Shuzhi also echoed this statement in the original trial, saying that although Wang Wu was a party member, he was not a Standing Committee member. Regarding Pu Yifan, they either said that there was another person, or that Pu Yifan was a mistake for Pu Yifang. Not only does this not match Xie Shaoshan's testimony, but it is also completely different from Chen Duxiu and Peng Shuzhi's statements in the investigation. There is no doubt that they are intentionally fabricating stories to protect Wang Wu and Pu Yifan. Therefore, it is difficult to adopt it as evidence beneficial to Wang Wu and Pu Yifan. Although Wang Zhaoqun and Guo Jinghao also do not admit to being in the same party as Chen Duxiu and others, Wang Zhaoqun was arrested for participating in the CCP Opposition's regular weekly meetings, as mentioned earlier. As for whether Wang Zhaoqun is named Luo Shifan and whether he is a Standing Committee member of the CCP Opposition, Chen Duxiu and Peng Shuzhi have repeatedly stated that Wei Shifan is not Wang Zhaoqun. Xie Shaoshan also did not specify that Luo Shifan was Wang Zhaoqun in the police station and the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court. Taking a look at the interaction, it can be determined that Wang Zhaoqun is only a member of the Central Opposition organization and not a Standing Committee member of that faction. Furthermore, Guo Jinghao's original name was Peng Daozhi, and he is Peng Shuzhi's younger brother. The original trial's prosecutor asked Peng Shuzhi, "Your brother is Peng Daozhi, is he in the party?" He replied, "Yes," which is sufficient to prove that Guo Jinghao is a member of the CCP Opposition. A detailed examination of the seized school registration form (i.e., the Communist Party registration form) shows that Peng Daozhi joined the group in Changsha, Hunan in September 1925 (1915 of the Republic), and then withdrew informally. In December 1929 (1918 of the Republic), he rejoined the Opposition in Shanghai. He had served as a district committee member and student movement leader in the Hudong district and is now responsible for organizational work and student movement, belonging to the Huxi district student branch. The remarks column states "Pseudonym Guo Jinghao" and although the three characters Guo Jinghao have been smeared out, they can still be recognized. It is clear that Guo Jinghao organized a group with the purpose of endangering the Republic, and the evidence is also very solid. There is no room for concealment. In summary, the original trial sentenced Wang Wu, Pu Yifan, and Wang Zhaoqun to five years of imprisonment each in accordance with Article 6 of the Emergency Law for the Punishment of Acts Endangering the Republic, and sentenced Guo Jinghao, who was considered young and ignorant and whose situation was pitiable, to two years and six months of imprisonment in accordance with Article 6, Article 10, and Article 77 of the same law, and Article 64 of the Criminal Law, and informed them of the standard for deducting imprisonment from the number of days of detention, which is not illegal. The various appeals of Wang Wu and others only deny the crime with empty words, which is unreasonable. After the Temporary Regulations for the Punishment of Counterrevolutionaries were abolished, the Emergency Law for the Punishment of Acts Endangering the Republic was a new law. Although there were provisions on the deprivation of civil rights in Article 11 of the Temporary Regulations for the Punishment of Counterrevolutionaries, the Emergency Law for the Punishment of Acts Endangering the Republic no longer adopts them. According to this court's precedent, anyone who violates the Emergency Law for the Punishment of Acts Endangering the Republic shall not be deprived of civil rights. However, the original trial deprived Chen Duxiu, Peng Shuzhi, Wang Wu, Pu Yifan, Wang Zhaoqun, and Guo Jinghao of their civil rights, which is clearly inappropriate and should be revoked by this court in its official capacity. Based on the above conclusions, in accordance with Article 409, Paragraph 1, Article 410, Paragraph 1, Section 1 of the Criminal Procedure Law, Article 2, Section 2, Article 6, Article 10 of the Emergency Law for the Punishment of Acts Endangering the Republic, Article 42, Article 74, Article 77, Article 80, Paragraph 2, Article 64, Article 60, Section 2 of the Criminal Law, Article 408, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Procedure Law, the judgment is as stated in the main text. June 30, 1934, Criminal Second Tribunal of the Supreme Court, Presiding Judge Xia Qinyin, Judge Yang Tianshou, Judge Gao Xi, Judge Zhang Fubing, Judge Zheng Chi. This true copy is certified to be identical to the original. Clerk Xia Juchu, July, 1934.

British troops in Shanhaiguan

The Exercises Will Continue

Japan Advocates for the Puppet State and Blocks British Military Exercises

Britain Ignores Protests Based on the Boxer Protocol

Seven Warships Cruise Between Qinhuangdao and Yuguan

A dispatch from Beiping reports that British forces are conducting exercises at Shanhaiguan. The Japanese side, advocating for the puppet state, has lodged a protest in an attempt to obstruct the exercises. However, the British military, refusing to recognize the puppet state, has dismissed the protest based on the Boxer Protocol. The two sides are at a standstill, and the issue remains unresolved. The background of this matter and the current situation are detailed below:

Article 9 of the Boxer Protocol states, "According to the clauses attached to the document of January 16, 1901, according to the Western calendar, i.e., November 26 of the previous year in the Chinese calendar, the Chinese government agrees that the countries concerned shall jointly determine the number of troops to be stationed in several locations to ensure that communication between the capital and the sea remains uninterrupted. The locations where the countries are stationed are Huangcun, Langfang, Yangcun, Tianjin, Junliangcheng, Tanggu, Lutai, Tangshan, Luanzhou, Changli, Qinhuangdao, and Shanhaiguan." According to this treaty, the countries stationed troops at the aforementioned locations. The number of troops stationed was usually the most from Britain, the United States, and Japan. Every autumn, foreign troops would choose a location for large-scale exercises. The American exercises were held at Qinhuangdao, and the British exercises were held at Shanhaiguan, which was the usual practice without any disputes. After Shanhaiguan was forcibly occupied by the Japanese military, it was returned, but the Great Wall was used as a boundary. The area of Yuguan outside the Great Wall was forcibly occupied by the Japanese as territory of the puppet state.

The British military exercises at the customs have always been in the Erlangmiao area outside the city. This year, in accordance with past practice, exercises are being held. The first exercise period was from August 1st to 3rd, for a total of three days. After the British military began its exercises, the Japanese side, wanting to advocate for the puppet state, came forward to obstruct them. In addition to protesting to the British military, they also notified the troops of various countries stationed in North China, claiming that the area outside Shanhaiguan belonged to the territory of the puppet state and that no army could arbitrarily conduct exercises without first notifying the Japanese side. The British military refused to accept the Japanese protest, replying that it had the right to station troops in Yuguan according to the Boxer Protocol, that exercises had been an established practice for many years, and that it only knew that it was Chinese territory and did not recognize any so-called puppet state. The language was very strong. The Japanese side, with its protest being ineffective, also conducted exercises in the Jiaoshan area, with a strong intention to demonstrate its power. At the same time, two British soldiers went missing, and rumors flourished for a time, and the situation suddenly became tense. Later, through mediation by various parties, a conflict was fortunately avoided. The British military exercises lasted for three days and ended on the 4th. At the same time, the two missing British soldiers were also found in Qinhuangdao on the 4th. The reason for the soldiers' disappearance is being kept secret by both sides and remains unclear.

Currently, this matter remains unresolved. The British military believes that it cannot abandon the treaty due to Japanese obstruction and will continue with the second exercise as originally planned from the 10th to the 15th of this month. Troops are being successively dispatched to Yuguan, and seven warships are cruising between Qinhuangdao and Yuguan. The commander of the British Navy, White, also went from Peiping to Qinhuangdao yesterday to inspect and then went to Yuguan. The Japanese side, seeing the British military's plan for a second exercise, also intends to conduct an equivalent exercise at the same time to show its opposition. It has dispatched six foreign warships to anchor in the waters of Qinhuangdao and the South Sea of Yuguan for surveillance. The commander of the fleet, Imamura, arrived in Lushun from Shanghai and then went to Yuguan to inspect the warships. In recent days, the situation between the two sides has been one of open and covert struggle (9th).

Hubei Province Disaster Area Reaches

Over 90 Million Mu

丨Grain Loss Exceeds 70 Million Yuan丨

A dispatch from Hankou states that Hubei Province has suffered exceptionally severe water and drought disasters this year, with the drought-stricken areas being especially widespread. As of now, the disaster area has reached 93,361,100 mu, with a grain loss of 25,974,290 dan. There are over ten million disaster victims, with about 2.8 million people in extreme poverty who rely entirely on relief. The alarming figures have exceeded the records of the past twenty years. Although the flood disaster is gradually subsiding, the drought disaster is becoming more severe. Some counties have not seen rain for three months and still have not received any rainfall. Thousands of miles of barren land and cries of despair can be heard everywhere, which is truly unbearable to witness and hear. In addition to sending telegrams to request relief, the provincial government has also formulated a fundamental disaster relief plan, setting up water pumps, installing siphons, opening up ponds and weirs, and dredging ditches, with 2.4 million yuan allocated for work relief. The Chairman of the Province, Zhang Qun, in order to implement this plan, specially took the "Ruihe" ship to Xunyang on the 9th, transferred to Lushan to meet with Director Wang and Chairman Jiang, reported the disaster situation, and requested relief. He will return to Hubei in about a week. Regarding the detailed situation of the disaster in each county, the Department of Civil Affairs has investigated and ascertained 39 counties, and on the 9th, it has submitted a list of the disaster area, population, and quantity and value of food losses to the provincial government. The counties affected by floods are Mianyang, Hanchuan, Tianmen, Zhongxiang, Jiangling, Lishan, Xiangyang, Yunxian, Jianshi, Zhijiang, Yunmeng, and other eleven counties. The counties affected by drought are Huang'an, Huangmei, Puqi, Xishui, Xianning, Huanggang, Macheng, Gong'an, Yicheng, Wuchang, Yangxin, Luotian, Huangpi, Xiaogan, Tongshan, Hanyang, Jiayu, Daye, Yidu, Songzi, Yingshan, Shishou, Qichun, Echeng, and twenty-four counties. The counties affected by water and drought disasters are Qianjiang, Tongcheng, Chongyang, Guangji, and other four counties.

At this time of severe drought, rice shortages have been reported in various counties, and unscrupulous merchants are taking the opportunity to manipulate prices, causing rice prices to soar, with each dan selling for eight or nine yuan. The price in Wuhan has risen by more than three yuan in a few days, and the current price is about ten yuan per dan. The city has only 300,000 dan of rice in stock, which is only enough for the citizens for twenty days. In addition to finding ways to stabilize prices, the government also convened a meeting of merchants and residents on the 9th to discuss relief measures, and it has been decided that rice merchants will raise funds to purchase rice from Hunan to maintain the people's food supply. However, Hunan is also suffering from disasters, and it is not yet known whether there will be surplus rice to help Hubei (9th).

Songjiang Temple Property Dispute: Buddhist Association Sends Telegrams to Petition

The Fenglong Temple outside the west gate of this city was approved by the Second Elementary School to be used as school buildings, which caused a dispute with the temple monk Lanfeng. The Public Security Bureau transferred both parties to await a court decision. The report from yesterday has been published. It is reported that the dispute over the Fenglong Temple is being contested by both sides. The monk filed an appeal to the Internal Affairs Department. Yesterday's report mistakenly stated that a judgment had been made. In fact, the Internal Affairs Department, after receiving the appeal, first ordered the county to stop the construction and wait for processing. However, yesterday, the school workers led the craftsmen to supervise the repair, causing another dispute. The local Buddhist Association, upon receiving the report, believes that the school is oppressing the monks and has decided to send a telegram to the provincial government's Internal Affairs Department to file an appeal and await a ruling. At the same time, it is requesting the central government to protect the interests of the monks.

Suzhou: Zhou Gu, Yu Shu Accuses Zhou Bingrong of Obstructing Freedom

Zhou Gu, Yu Shu, a woman from Tongli, Wujiang, is 28 years old. In the 16th year of the Republic of China, she married Zhou Bingrong, who is currently serving as a prosecutor at the Changxing District Court in Zhejiang. She had previously filed a complaint with the Wujiang County Court, accusing her husband of obstructing freedom and abandonment, and attached a civil suit, requesting a judgment ordering them to live together and a one-time payment of 1,000 yuan for reputational damage. Zhou Bingrong also filed a petition with Wujiang County, requesting a judgment ordering a divorce from Gu. After a hearing, the court ruled Zhou Bingrong not guilty. Zhou Gu, Yu Shu, dissatisfied with the judgment, came to Suzhou to appeal to the Women's Association, requesting assistance, and hired lawyer Song Mingdong to file an appeal with the Wuxian District Court. The appeal stated that on September 24th of last year, the defendant called the appellant into the room, closed the door, threatened her with a gun, and ordered the appellant to copy a divorce document that he had written in advance, which stated that the appellant had a vague relationship with Ren Xiaohe and Ren Chuanquan and voluntarily severed the relationship with her husband. The appellant, being unable to resist, had no choice but to copy the document. Now, the appellant presents the handwritten divorce draft snatched from Zhou Bingrong as evidence. Since then, the appellant has been abandoned and ignored. The appellant now suffers from third-stage lung disease and is unable to support herself. The original judgment is unfair and should be overturned to order the defendant to live with the appellant and pay a one-time fee of 1,000 yuan for reputational damage. After the court approved the appeal, it held a hearing at 11:00 a.m. yesterday (the 10th). Zhou Gu, Yu Shu arrived at the court with lawyer Song. Zhou Bingrong did not attend and was represented by lawyers Zhu Fucheng and Tao Jianshan. The lawyers presented a note written by Zhou Gu, Yu Shu, stating that she sought help from the City God because she had a physical relationship with Ren Xiaohe and a relationship with Ren Chuanquan and felt sorry for her husband, now realizing her remorse and asking for forgiveness. Zhou Gu, Yu Shu said that the note was also written under duress by the defendant. The court ordered Zhou Bingrong to be summoned to court for further verification.

Nantong County Magistrate Escorted for Handover

The former Nantong County Magistrate Zhuang Yan has not been able to settle the handover of duties for a long time. Zhuang is currently residing in Suzhou. The Wuxian County Magistrate received an order from the Finance Department yesterday (the 10th), ordering a political police officer to go to Zhuang's residence to escort Zhuang Yan to Nantong to settle the handover of duties.

Wuxi Autumn Silkworm Instructors Depart for Work

The two directors of the local sericulture model area, Yan and Jiang, believing that the autumn silkworm season is about to begin and that the rural autumn planting instructors should go to the countryside to work, specifically ordered them to depart yesterday (the 10th). They also convened a meeting of all instructors the day before yesterday to hold a discussion. They first sent letters to people in the silk and cocoon industry to come and provide guidance. The County Magistrate Yan Shenyu, the Director of the Provincial Sericulture Experiment Station Tang Xixiang, the technician of the Construction Department Xiong Qixian, and the Director of the County Agricultural Extension Institute Shen Xichun gave speeches until about 12:00 p.m. In the afternoon, the central instructors convened meetings of instructors from various townships to discuss the various preparations for going to the countryside. Yesterday morning (the 10th), all the instructors departed for the countryside to work. In addition, due to the implementation of the unified management method for this year's autumn planting, the sericulture model area has established a silkworm seed sales office, which is scheduled to start selling on the 15th.

Changzhou Finance Department Sends Personnel to Investigate Miscellaneous Taxes

The Jiangsu Finance Department has dispatched Yan Shudong to Changzhou to investigate the collection of miscellaneous taxes and handle the collection of deed taxes. According to Commissioner Yan, the investigation results are satisfactory. However, the banquet tax and the capital contribution tax in Wujin should also be collected uniformly by the county government to comply with the regulations. The county government has been instructed to do so. In addition, the fishing tax and the drama tax should be abolished and the collection should be stopped in accordance with the method of abolishing harsh and miscellaneous taxes. Commissioner Yan finished the investigation and went to Suzhou on the evening of the 9th for further investigation before returning to the department to report.

Changshu Guard Team Leader Replaced

The county guard team has only been reorganized and established for three months. In addition to the county magistrate serving as the commander-in-chief, Fan Zhengshan, commissioned by the province, served as the deputy commander-in-chief. In the middle of last month, representatives sent by Jiang inspected various places. The county participated in the Wuxi district exercises. Under the inspection of the commissioners, they believed that the guard team's academics and maneuvers were not very good, which was due to the deputy commander-in-chief Fan Zhengshan's poor training. Therefore, an order was issued on the 9th to transfer Fan to the province. The vacancy was filled by Zhu Lianfang, who is an instructor from the Provincial Security Office.

Jiangyin: Locust Nymphs Cover the Fields in Four Townships

Since the beginning of summer, due to the drought and lack of rain, locust nymphs have occurred in the Yangku Huashu area of the eastern township and have invaded the paddy fields, causing serious damage. Recently, the county government received reports from the villagers of various districts and townships that locust nymphs are everywhere in Yunting Huangtang and other townships and have bitten off the nearby crops, causing farmers to panic. However, the district and township chiefs are only verbally calling for action and have no solution. The situation is likely to spread throughout the county. Yesterday (the 8th), County Magistrate Bao specifically sent Ji Yuqi, a technician from the Agricultural Extension Institute, to go to the countryside to investigate first. The drought relief association also raised the price to buy locust nymphs, 300 yuan per catty for locust nymphs and 200 yuan per catty for flying locusts. County Magistrate Bao also decided to personally go to the countryside to inspect various districts in the coming days.

Zhenjiang Water Police Captain Shelters Opium Smugglers and Flees in Fear of Punishment

The third detachment of the fifteenth team of the fourth district of the Water Police has been stationed at the port. Ligang Port, under its jurisdiction, has always been a transit area for opium. It has been heard that the current captain of the detachment, Sun Jiesan, since taking office, has joined forces with local natives and the security corps to smuggle opium, openly accepting illicit fees without any scruples. However, the matter was not kept secret and was learned by the province and Captain Xu, who sent personnel to verify it. The Provincial Security Office sent a team to the area to disarm all the team police and the security corps and sent them to the province for legal action. The captain of the detachment, Sun Jie, learned of the situation in advance and fled in fear of punishment. Captain Xu, considering that the duties were related, specifically supervised the dispatch of Fan Zuyu, a clerk from the brigade headquarters, to act as the captain of the detachment. Fan plans to go to take office today (the 10th) after being commissioned.

Haimen Seizes a Large Batch of Opium

Since the strict prohibition of opium pills in the county, the sales of opium have increased sharply, and opium dealers have taken the opportunity to become active again. The day before yesterday (the 7th) at about 10:00 p.m., a large batch of opium was brought from Shanghai to Haimen by the Xinrenhe ship and unloaded at Xingang and handed over to Chen Cai Gou by boat. However, it was detected by the county Public Security Bureau, which immediately sent inspector Ding Zuozhou and many police officers to search. They seized two sacks containing two large packages of opium and brought the boatman Chen Cai Gou back to the bureau for interrogation. Yesterday (the 8th), they were sent to the county government for investigation.

San Chang City Fire

Yuan Futai's tofu shop in Donghou Street, San Chang City, owned by Yuan Zuomei, burned grass clippings in the cowshed to drive away flies and mosquitoes at about 2:00 p.m. yesterday (the 7th). Carelessly, the fire spread to the reed wall, and suddenly thick smoke and raging flames engulfed the city, shocking the entire city. The fire brigade of the Dasheng Third Factory and the industrial security team all set out to rescue the situation. However, due to the long period of drought, the ditches were dry and it was difficult to get water. In addition, most of the nearby houses were thatched cottages, so the fire spread westward and was difficult to contain. Subsequently, nearby villagers and factory workers rushed to help with the rescue, and the fire gradually went out around 4:00 p.m. It is estimated that more than twenty houses were destroyed, with losses of about 10,000 yuan.

Female Student Commits Suicide Due to Failing a Grade

Wang Xizeng's second daughter, Zhuoru, 19 years old, from Gaojia Town, Qidong, was a student at the Shanghai Wuben Girls' School. In this summer's exam, her grades were not good, and she failed to move up a grade. After returning home, she was repeatedly scolded by her parents, which made her feel ashamed and hateful. She then had thoughts of ending her life and bought one yuan of opium the day before yesterday, secretly swallowing it. Soon after, she was poisoned, her face turned pale, and she groaned incessantly. After her parents noticed, they rushed her to the Dasheng Hospital in Jiulong Town for treatment, but the poisoning was too deep to be saved, and she soon died.

Murderer of Hangzhou Leashed Military Officer Escorted to Hangzhou

Li Chuhua, an accountant from the third branch of the Zhejiang Provincial Security Office, came to the province on March 6th of this year to collect 2,500 yuan in military pay and stayed at the Wuhe Hotel in the city station. Unexpectedly, he was strangled to death by the conscript Wang Qinggen in the middle of the night, who fled with the money. It is now learned that the murderer Wang Qinggen sneaked back to his home in Hunan and was arrested and escorted. More than 600 yuan of the stolen money was still on him. Chairman Lu reported the matter and sent a commissioner to escort him to Zhejiang for interrogation by the fourth section of the Security Office and to be dealt with according to law.

Collapsed City Wall Crushes a Laborer to Death

Ying Jilin, 36 years old, from Pujiang, made a living as a laborer. At 8:00 a.m. yesterday, he was supposed to go to the city wall on Huancheng West Road, West Street, to dig and carry mud. Unexpectedly, the city wall suddenly collapsed and he was crushed into the rubble. His companions managed to rescue him, but his left abdomen had become a large hole, with intestines flowing out. He died on the spot. The Public Security Bureau called the Hangzhou Land Court to send an official for inspection, bought a coffin, and prepared for burial.

Traffic Accident on West Street

At the Dache Bridge area of West Street, Hangzhou City, at 1:00 p.m. on the 9th, a No. 1122 vehicle on Route 6 of the Highway Bureau, driven by driver Sun Ziwen, passed through the area. The driver braked to avoid pedestrians and knocked down a No. 3048 rickshaw. The rickshaw puller Liang Hongyao suffered injuries to his waist and legs, which seemed quite serious. The passenger Hu Zhu was also injured in the face. The passenger in the car, Zhang Baohua, fell and lost two front teeth due to the impact. The police officer on duty saw that an accident had occurred and immediately detained the driver and sent the injured to the hospital for treatment. It is reported that the rickshaw puller Liang Hongyao was seriously injured and his life may be in danger.

City News of This City

City Chamber of Commerce Sends Letter to Guangdong Chamber of Commerce

To Assist in Abolishing Special Taxes on National Goods

Even if the Purpose is to Sanction Foreign Factories

National Goods Manufacturers Should Not Be Affected

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce sent another letter to the Guangzhou Chamber of Commerce yesterday, saying: "Dear Sirs, on the 9th of this month, we received a letter from the enamelware industry association stating that, according to a letter from members such as Huafeng Enamelware Company, Guangzhou customers claim that Guangzhou is currently experiencing industrial decline, with many large factories closing down one after another. Those that are struggling to survive are also in a precarious situation. The local authorities, recognizing the precariousness of industry and commerce, convened the city's chamber of commerce to discuss measures to maintain it. A plan was discussed and agreed upon to establish a bureau to collect taxes on imported goods and goods entering from outside the province, such as paint, enamel, copper, iron, hardware, rubber, matches, etc., all of which are included in the collection. The industrial and commercial sectors, citing that many Shanghai factories are invested in by foreigners and dump their products in Guangdong, requested the authorities to implement taxes to protect the province's industry. It is heard that the authorities are considering this matter, and it is likely to be implemented. If it is implemented, it will be greatly disadvantageous to the shipping of goods from Shanghai factories. We hope that you will forward a letter to the city chamber of commerce to strongly argue with the Guangdong provincial authorities to alleviate the difficulties of the Shanghai merchants, etc.' We have received this. We have checked that Shanghai's business relies entirely on exports. If heavy taxes are levied on national goods, it will cut off the circulation of national goods. Once implemented, Shanghai's commerce will be greatly affected. We should report the situation to your association and quickly argue with the Guangdong provincial authorities based on reason, striving to abolish this agreement to benefit the progress of national goods.' We received this letter. We checked that we had previously received a letter from the China Chemical Industry Association with the same situation. The company had previously sent a letter with the same information and the chamber of commerce should send a telegram to the Southwest Political Affairs Committee, the Guangdong Provincial Government, if the matter of special taxes is inevitable, please follow the example of the Pito Special Tax Bureau, draw a clear line to ensure that the national factories are not implicated in the case. Now that this matter has been suggested by the industrial and commercial sectors of your province, the strategy of mediation depends entirely on your association. In recent years, the precariousness of industry and commerce is not limited to Guangdong Province, but is a common phenomenon throughout the country. The strategy to save it is to work together, share resources, and resist the dumping of foreign goods. If we first divide the provincial boundaries and strengthen their defenses, making it difficult for goods from Province A to be sold in Province B, the scope of commercial activity will become narrower, which is tantamount to suicide, (omitted) The suggestors in your province are also worried that this move will involve coercion, so they use the term 'many Shanghai factories are invested in by foreigners' to conceal the truth from the public and make it easier for this case to be established. In commercial ports, foreigners have the right to set up factories in accordance with the Treaty of Shimonoseki. If other places hear the news and respond, saying that the industrial and commercial products of the commercial ports of Guangdong and Shantou in your province are mostly invested in by foreigners, and they collect taxes as an example, how will you deal with it? It seems that such indiscriminate and sweeping wording will cause endless malpractices. We have checked that in Shanghai, only the textile factory has more foreign investment, and the cigarette factory has more foreign power. As for paint, cosmetics, enamel, rubber, matches and other factories, there are fewer foreign investments, and most of them are set up by Chinese. There are registration documents from the Ministry of Industry to prove the establishment of the company, and there are membership lists to check when joining the association. Now, your province does not pay attention to the two industries of textiles and cigarettes, which are more powerful by foreign businessmen, but only pays attention to the various industries of paint and cosmetics, which are less related to foreign businessmen. This is probably to avoid the heavy responsibility and avoid negotiations. When this special tax is implemented, it will take more effort to clarify that a certain factory is not a foreign factory. We would like to suggest that your association suggest to the authorities in your province to send personnel to Shanghai to investigate before holding the event, and to investigate with our association which is the Chinese factory and which is not, so as to distinguish and handle the matter to avoid national goods manufacturers from being affected in the same way, which is the most important thing.

Lin Kanghou Talks About the US Collecting Silver for Nationalization

Will Not Affect Our Country

Silver Outflow is Entirely Due to Trade Deficit

Huadong News Agency reported that the US government's announcement that silver will be collected for nationalization has caused drastic changes in the global gold and silver markets. As China is a silver-using country, it has a vital interest in this issue. A reporter from the Huadong News Agency visited Lin Kanghou, Secretary-General of the Banking Association, yesterday. According to Lin's observation on this matter, it is difficult to predict what benefits or harms the US's collection of silver for nationalization will have on us. However, the general public believes that this move will cause gold to fall and silver to soar, and that a large amount of silver in our country will flow out, which will not become a reality. This is because China's silver outflow recently is not due to the rise in silver prices. The real reason is purely due to the trade deficit of foreign goods in recent years. Since foreign goods have been imported in large quantities, and Chinese merchants are unable to lower the cost of Chinese exports when calculating the price of goods, it is inevitable that silver will be used to pay for the price of goods. Therefore, under this situation, China's silver outflow is difficult to curb. The fundamental solution depends on the self-strengthening of national goods, so that the trade deficit can be easily changed into a trade surplus, and the silver in the country will not flow out.

The Municipal Government Invited Various Groups Yesterday

to Hold a Wusong River Dredging Conference

It Was Decided to Spend 200,000 Yuan

The municipal government believes that the Wusong River has a significant impact on farmland. At 10:00 a.m. yesterday, it invited the Finance Bureau, Public Works Bureau, Labor Bureau, etc., as well as the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and the Shipping Industry Association, to discuss dredging measures in the municipal government conference room in the city center. Xu Peihuang, director of the Public Works Bureau, Cai Zengji, director of the Political Affairs Bureau, Shen Yi, director of the Labor Bureau, Pan Xusheng of the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, and Wang Bofen, Yang Youlong, and Wan Yongsheng of the Shanghai Shipping Industry Association attended. Secretary-General Yu Hongjun chaired the meeting and reported on the dredging of the Wusong River, which affects the water conservancy of eight counties: Shangbao, Suzhou, Songjiang, Jiading, Taicang, Kunshan, Qingpu. It is a pity that it has not been dredged for many years, and the river channel is becoming increasingly silted up. The mayor deeply appreciates this and specifically convened various relevant agencies to discuss dredging measures. Then, the discussion began, and it was decided on the spot that (1) the cost of dredging the Wusong River was set at 200,000 yuan, and the Public Works Bureau would prepare a detailed dredging plan; (2) the municipal government would allocate 50,000 yuan, and the remaining 150,000 yuan would be raised by the Municipal Chamber of Commerce by inviting various relevant groups. The meeting ended at 12:00 p.m.
