Letters to the Editor

To the Editor: In today's news column of your newspaper, there is an item about the loan dispute between the Bank of Communications, Fu Xiao'an, and lawyer Yan Dajue, which states that Dai Zhenwu, also known as Shengzu, a relative of Wang and a small proprietor of the Nissho Taisei Shipping Company, borrowed more than 110,000 yuan from the Bank of Communications on behalf of Fu to plan expenses. Dai signed the promissory note, which was kept in Wang's vault. After Wang Xinguan's death last year, Fu also had the arrest warrant cancelled, so he returned to his original position. Fu then convened a board meeting at the bank and presented this promissory note, intending to sue Dai for the previous loan. Although the directors did not agree with his proposal, Fu insisted strongly.

All of the above is untrue. The so-called "planning expenses on behalf of Fu" and "Fu insisting strongly on suing" are all fabrications by Dai Zhenwu as a pretext for intimidation, which are not worth a knowing person's smile. However, your newspaper's report used assertive language, which inevitably confuses rumors. Therefore, I am writing to request that your newspaper correct this matter as soon as possible. Respectfully submitted to the Editorial Department of Shen Bao, Lawyer Dai Chengxiang, August 10th. To the Editor: After reading the corrected news item about the Jiyutai Silk Factory in your newspaper's letter samples on the 9th, I was extremely surprised. According to the news of the suspension of work at the three silk factories issued by our agency on July 30, it was obtained from interviews with the silk workers' union in the Sixth District and after personally visiting each of the silk factories for on-site investigation. The Jiyu Silk Factory was indeed shut down. After reading the correction message yesterday, I went to the silk factory to inquire, and the accountant Mr. Xu replied that the factory was shut down for a few days last month because the cocoons were out of stock, and resumed work on August 2nd. Therefore, when our agency published the news, the factory was indeed in the period of shutdown. On the 7th of this month, the economic news columns of various newspapers also carried news of the factory's shutdown. The factory actually claimed that it had never been interrupted, and I don't know what its intention is. It is a matter of our agency's reputation and should be published in the letter column to clarify the truth. We are truly grateful. Respectfully submitted to the Editorial Department of Shen Bao, Dagong News Agency, August 10th.

Reading Questions and Answers

Continued "Errors and Difficulties in Translations" (Third Continuation)

| Reply to Mr. Duroki |

Answer: That is to say, "Instead of enriching abstract thinking with practical content, all practical aspects are dispersed (abandoned), leaving only abstract thinking."

Question: On page 257, under the heading "Qualitative Differences in Various Stages of Development in a Certain Process," does this mean that the fundamental qualities will not differ, but rather the differences in non-essential qualities (i.e., the so-called secondary qualities)? For example, the book cites the four periods of the Soviet Union, from the era of wartime communism to the current era of socialism. Presumably, this is a development of the fundamental quality, just like the development of the three periods of capitalism, without daring to change the fundamental quality. However, why does the book (page 257, line 3) also say: "Each stage has its own different qualities?" Then, ultimately, is the fundamental quality of each stage of development different, or is it just the development of the particularity of quality?

Answer: The term "fundamental" is a relative term. The qualities of each stage of capitalism, in relation to the entire process of capitalism, are "secondary qualities." However, in relation to each stage itself, they are the fundamental, primary qualities. When we take the entire development of capitalism as the subject of study, we say that each stage is distinguished by a kind of "secondary quality." When we take the differences between stages as the subject of study, we say that each stage differs in its fundamental characteristics. This is one of the contradictions of things themselves. Failure to understand this contradiction, and insisting on strictly distinguishing between "fundamental" and "secondary," will result in falling into metaphysical error.

Question: "…do not allow Soviet economic accumulation to achieve a development speed above that of capitalist economies." Is the character "爲" (wéi) in this sentence a mistake for "以" (yǐ)? If not, please explain.

Answer: The character "爲" is not wrong. The character "不" (bù) above the character "爲" is a typesetting error and should be changed to the character "以" (yǐ).

Question: "...the transformation from one stage of development to another is a leap." For example, the transformation from the commercial capital era to the industrial capital stage in capitalism also requires a revolution?

Answer: Revolution is the overthrow of old relations of production or class relations. Although the various stages of capitalism have leaps, they also involve sacrifices (such as the overthrow of small-scale production by large-scale production), but it is not a revolution.

Question: "The essence is not fully expressed in a single phenomenon. Therefore, the phenomenon is richer and more complete than the essence it expresses." I don't understand.

Answer: "It" refers to "phenomenon." The essence is not expressed by a single phenomenon, but by a variety of phenomena. There is only one essence, but there are many expressions of phenomena. Therefore, phenomena are more abundant, richer, and more complete than essence. (End)

Free Talk

On Europeanization

— Huang Huaibai

In this era of daily contact between all of humanity, there are still some Chinese people who feel great disgust and contempt when Europeanization is mentioned. The reason for this is simple: so-called "Europeanization" is "different" from our original things. Because of this, under the dominance of feudal consciousness and restoration movements, certain groups of Chinese people always find things that are "different" from us to be unpleasant. Because it is not pleasing to the eye, it arouses a sense of jealousy and opposition, which is only natural. As for the good or bad of Europeanization itself, that is another question. Apart from firing a few cold arrows with a mocking attitude, no one has ever faithfully assessed the true value of "Europeanization." The opposition to Europeanization by such people is still the same psychology as the Boxers thirty years ago, only with a difference in degree. There is another kind of person who feels that European things, although relatively rationalized and modernized, are good, but we are ultimately descendants of the Yellow Emperor, and the national essence must be preserved, and the way of the former kings must be defended. For example, the great master of traditional Chinese learning, Mr. Wang Renqiu, when he saw the foreign devils' steamships and cannons, compared to our own sailboats and earth cannons, could not help but feel inferior. However, in order to preserve the national essence, Mr. Wang issued the following wonderful argument:

"Steamships are the most clumsy of ships. Foreign cannons are the most stupid of things. Ships should be light and nimble, and weapons should be ingenious and convenient. Now, foreign ships cannot move until the coal fire is lit; cannons must be carried by people, and are too heavy to lift. If a decisive person dares to approach them suddenly, they will lose their support and be left with their hands tied, waiting for death." - Memorandum on Handling Foreign Affairs

We can still hear this kind of argument against Europeanization today.

However, the facts are facts after all. Everything in China is too "ancient." In the current world, it is impossible to continue to be "ancient" for a long time. So what should be done? Undoubtedly, it needs new life to transform it. This so-called new life, I dare to boldly say, is to "Europeanize" as much as possible within our possible range.

What is the basic spirit of Europeanization? Previous generations have already given us various explanations. For example, Mr. Science (Science) and Mr. Democracy (Democracy), which were advocated by the general public during the "May Fourth" era, are better explanations of "Europeanization." However, according to my personal observation, I believe that the basic spirit of Europeanization is "progress." In other words, Europeanization is modernization, and opposing Europeanization is tantamount to clinging to bones and challenging everything modern. Assuming that my observation is not wrong, and that China cannot return from the modern era to the era of the Yellow Emperor, then where will it go? Undoubtedly, there is only one way! Europeanization. Literature, which occupies a corner position in the entire cultural history of China, is of course no exception.

Speaking of the Europeanization of literature, opponents use the excuse that literature is based on language and writing. China has its own independent language and writing. Lacking this basic condition for Europeanization, and yet talking about the Europeanization of literature, the result will inevitably become a non-descript literature. This argument seems to be true, but it is not. Because the advocacy of the Europeanization of literature is to bring some Western styles and modern sentiments into this stagnant Chinese literature. Specifically: it is to transform low-level works such as *Nine-tailed Turtle* and *Unofficial History of the Scholars* into *La Dame aux Camélias* by Alexandre Dumas fils. To transform works such as *Seven Heroes and Five Gallants* and *Wild River Heroine* into *Don Quixote* by Cervantes. To transform the ballad of gifting gold in the garden and secretly making a life-long agreement into *A Doll's House* by Ibsen. To change the shallow humor of joking and teasing into the humor of Shaw. To transform works that describe the dark aspects of society, such as the *XX Black Curtain Grand View*, into *The Jungle* and *King Coal* by Sinclair. To transform works such as *A Guide to Love Letters* into *Julie, or the New Heloise* by Rousseau. This is the meaning of Europeanization. In summary: Chinese literature is like a temple that has been in disrepair for a long time, and the beams and pillars inside are crooked and decayed. Therefore, on the eve of this storm, new materials and new construction methods are needed to change the old appearance and make it a more solemn and splendid building. The purpose of our advocacy of the Europeanization of literature lies in this.

Finally, to avoid misunderstanding by the general public, it must be stated: "Europeanization" is different from "enslavement." The upper-class Chinese people on the Shanghai Bund often look down on Chinese people, and the newly arrived gilded doctors do not like to speak Chinese very much. When these people go to the village, dressed in Western clothes and leather shoes, facing people who cannot get fritters and pancakes, they eat their chocolate and waltz with their lovers, and complain that the floor in the countryside is not as smooth as the floor in the city. So, they cannot help but sigh and say: "China is too backward! It is hopeless!" People like this can be said to be "enslaved." What we call "Europeanization" is absolutely different from this. Therefore, we want to advocate "Europeanization" in the active aspect, and in the passive aspect, we want to prevent "enslavement."

Borderland Night Records (Part 2)

— Wu Yan

The brothers of the business protection team widened their eyes and made a gesture of dragging people away.

"Good, good, good, our captain is going to take you, bandit!"

The man with the beard became even more angry and bumped straight towards the outside.

"Who are you scaring? Who are you scaring? I've been to even Military Governor X's mansion, and his wife is still...!!"

"What military governor or not, I don't care so much! Are you blind? Look, this is our territory!"

The brothers of the business protection team put their guns on their backs, also quickened their pace, interrupted the man's words, and shouted loudly as they went out. The old woman leaned against the door, anxious and crying.

"Oh, soldiers, please spare us... Teacher, teacher, let it go, let it go!"

"Don't be afraid! Don't be afraid! I've met all kinds of officials!"

Outside the door in the darkness, a voice full of vitality was sent back, and it seemed that a look of belief appeared on the old woman's face, but I was uneasy and worried about the bearded man. Because I had seen the captain's temper very clearly along the way. I remember resting in a mountain family's home, and some of the younger brothers attacked the dry land, taking a large portion of the corn from the people's land, throwing it into the fire to make a meal. The old woman, her daughter-in-law, and her grandson all ran over and knelt in front of the captain, crying for justice and demanding compensation. The captain, while drinking the wine from the bottle and eating the dried beef, opened his drunken red eyes and cursed wildly.

"What is a little corn? Hmph, you deserve to be robbed by bandits, get out of here!"

The old woman saw that I was pondering and asked me:

"Guest, you've seen the captain, he wouldn't beat our teacher, would he?"

I didn't want to scare her, so I said that the captain was also very fair, and immediately talked about her teacher. Because it was very strange to me that an old woman of her age still had such a strange teacher. She slightly straightened her white hair and slowly said:

"Ah, everything needs the teacher, without the teacher's guidance, even walking down that road is like bumping around blindly. This, how would I understand? Later, Granny Wang told me, Zhang Dama, how can you do this? Eating vegetarian food all your life, and worshiping the Bodhisattva all your life, is also in vain. You have to find a teacher to teach you... Oh, guest, you must be hungry! I've been talking, you can go to the kitchen to cook rice yourself!"

I said:

"Let me rest for a while, and I'll go cook later."

She took out a small basket of string beans herself, slightly tilted her head, and while tearing off the strings of the string beans, continued to speak.

"I think about it, her old woman's words are really right, why did my two sons die on the front line? It's just that the Bodhisattva doesn't know that I'm doing good deeds, and the good deeds I do don't count!... Oh, you sit, I'm enough to tear myself, don't help me... Now that I'm worshiping the teacher, I'm willing to spend a little more money!"

When she said the last sentence. A happy smile floated on her lips, and at the same time, her eyes turned towards the painted image of Guanyin, and she raised her happy eyes again.

At this time, I gradually understood that the bearded man was probably a Qi Gong of a benevolent hall, who came to preach and teach in the countryside, so I asked casually:

"Old mother, how much does it cost to worship the teacher?"

"Uh, I can't tell others this!"

The old woman lowered her head very seriously and suddenly discovered a string bean with worms.

"Oh, look, it looks good on the outside... people are like this too!"

Shaking her head, she immediately raised a melancholy face, opened her pleading eyes, and looked at the deity on the wall again. But I still asked.

"Why can't you tell people?"

She showed a slightly embarrassed look, scratched her head with her fingertips for a while, and said:

"The teacher said that people in the world are unreliable, and you can't tell them anything..."

Just then, the bearded man came back, with a happy look on his face, and threw something like a brick on the table. The old woman hurriedly grabbed it in her hand, happily shouted like she had found a treasure:

"Oh! It's still brought back?"

I asked curiously:

"What is this!"

"Hey, don't you know? This is salt."

The bearded man replied, and at the same time, as if he couldn't help but be happy, he said:

"Ha, what captain, really! When I went in, he was very majestic and wanted to eat people. How could I know that when I mentioned Commander Hu and Commander Zhang, he changed his face all of a sudden, haha, tonight is really interesting!"

The old woman also said happily, panting:

"Tonight is really the Bodhisattva's eyes!"

"Yes, it all depends on the gods above!"

The bearded man followed, immediately clasped his hands in front of his chest, raised his head, and made an indistinct sound in his mouth, as if he was chanting a spell. Then he called the old woman to kneel in front of the Guanyin statue and shout:

"One bow... Another bow... Three bows..."

While offering incense. Outside the house was a quiet night, only the sound of horses neighing was heard in the distance. (End)

Impressions of Zibo

— Luo San

(8) Going to Shantou

In order to collect pottery samples, I asked Mr. Zhang of the local People's Education Center to be my guide for a trip to Shantou.

Shantou is located five or six li from Boshan City and is the center of porcelain production in Boshan. (It is said that in addition to this, Fushan, Xihe, Badou, Yaoguang, Beiling, Wudian, Wuzi and other places are also porcelain producing areas, but they are not as large in scale as Shantou.) At its peak, there were more than 200 porcelain businesses there, and 20,000 to 30,000 people relied on the porcelain industry for a living! Now, however, it has declined considerably!

We walked along the Xiaofu River and boarded a small coal train next to Lingquan Temple, traveling on a narrow-gauge railway. We advanced along the ridges and slopes! Speaking of this narrow-gauge railway, it is quite interesting. It was originally built by several private individuals and runs directly from Badou to Zhangbo Station. It can transport coal from Bodong and other companies to the main railway station. (There is currently talk of selling it to the Jiaoji Railway Committee.) The train is half the size of an ordinary train, but much larger than the narrow-gauge railways used for building roads! But don't let its small appearance fool you, it earns 1,000 yuan a day transporting coal. And workers sell passenger tickets at each station. For a few copper coins or two or three dimes, one can travel twenty or thirty li on a "convenience route"! This income is considered the workers' profit and is not related to the railway authorities! However, the carriages of the small train have no latches at the joints, only iron hooks and iron rings, so sometimes when going downhill, inertia pulls the rear carriages forward, and there is a danger of the rings coming loose, and overturning is commonplace! So, when we got on, we thought, "Once on the train, our lives are handed over to the iron rings until we get off!"

Fortunately, it was only two small stations to Shantou, and our lives were able to get off safely.

Arriving at Shantou, we saw a forest of kiln chimneys! We went to a workshop to take a look around and asked them for some raw materials such as porcelain clay, body clay, and axles, as well as finished bodies and objects.

They make bowls, teapots, plates, vases, etc., but they are all rough pieces, far inferior to Jiangxi goods and Western goods!

Their making of bodies, glazing, and painting are purely manual, without the use of modern machinery! It is said that in the past, these porcelain wares were sold in large quantities in the Northeast. People in the Northeast often used Shantou porcelain as dowry. Since the fall of the Northeast, business has plummeted! The number of existing kiln households has decreased from 200 to 50 or 60! Shantou used to be a famous workers' district, with more than a dozen large restaurants, but now there are none. Workers who paint porcelain patterns used to earn one yuan a day for children and two or three yuan for adults: now it's over! Wages are low and few people are employed! The problem of unemployment is pressing down on the people of Boshan!

In Boshan, we can see the decline of China's small handicrafts and the defects of the social system! Undoubtedly, the power of international capitalism overwhelms all aspects of Chinese life! Do Chinese people still have the ability to struggle? I sighed like this on the coal train back.

The Old Man (1)

— Jin Yi

The shop that hung the sign "Aksakov's Old Goods and Sundries" was squeezed on a street full of such businesses. The gold lettering on the sign above the door had already lost its golden color, and the strokes of the characters, which were made of mud, had been eroded by years of rain, making it easy for people to read it as "Aksakov's Old Goods and Sundries," or "Aax Aksakov's Old Goods and Sundries." But such misreadings were only by newcomers, because this shop had been on this street for thirty years.

To the right of the shop was a low-grade restaurant, marked as selling a "Hometown Lunch" for twenty-five cents a serving (in fact, most of the customers in Xingli were beggars who spent five cents to buy a soup and soaked the bread they had begged for in the soup); on the left was another old goods shop. The street was dirty, with swarms of flies flying around in the summer, so many that the buzzing sound could make one's head spin; but in the winter, a layer of ice and snow covered everything, not only hiding all the filth inside, making it look quite clean; but also making the uneven road, which had never been repaired since it was built, seem smooth. But this smoothness was not beneficial to pedestrians, but made it easier for them to fall on it.

This day was the evening of January 15th, and those stateless White Russian people had just spent their New Year the day before. Every festive day made it easier for them to remember everything that had happened in the past, because in fact it would never happen again, so they felt it was more worth cherishing.

Page 13

Education News: This Year's Private Colleges and Universities

Approved Budget for Subsidies

The National Treasury Allocates 60,000 Yuan Monthly

Totaling 720,000 Yuan Annually

A Total of 32 Schools Approved

Starting this year, the National Treasury will allocate 720,000 yuan annually to private colleges and universities as subsidies. This matter is of great importance to the development of higher education, and all parties attach great importance to it. Although the distribution of this subsidy for this year has not been officially announced, it has been completely decided. Recently, our reporter has made detailed inquiries about the process of the Ministry of Education handling this matter, and the information obtained is as follows:

In March of this year, in order to encourage private colleges and universities with excellent performance and financial difficulties, the Ministry of Education proposed to the Executive Yuan that starting from the 23rd year of the Republic, the National Treasury should allocate 60,000 yuan monthly, totaling 720,000 yuan annually, as the amount of subsidies for private colleges and universities, stating that emphasis should be placed on practical subjects when providing subsidies, and the amount of subsidies should not be less than 70 percent, and the subsidy items should be equipment costs and faculty costs. This was subsequently approved by the Executive Yuan and the Central Political Council. The Central Political Council also suggested that attention should be paid to the degree of educational development in the region when determining the standards for subsidies, and that efforts should be made to make it universal throughout the country, without favoring certain areas. After the Ministry of Education formulated the Outline of the Measures for the Distribution of Subsidies to Private Colleges and Universities and submitted it to the Executive Yuan and the Central Political Council for approval and filing, it immediately issued a notice to all private colleges and universities across the country stating that those who wished to apply for subsidies this year should submit their applications to the Ministry before the end of June in accordance with the provisions of the Outline of the Measures for the Distribution of Subsidies. A total of 41 schools applied for subsidies. At the same time, in accordance with the provisions of the Outline of the Measures, the Review Committee was organized, and seven expert members from outside the Ministry who had no relationship with private universities and members appointed from within the Ministry were hired. The Review Committee meetings were held for one week starting from July 23. The Review Committee handled this matter with great caution. First, it discussed and determined the review standards as follows: (1) Subsidies are limited to those with excellent performance and financial difficulties (based mainly on inspection reports); (2) The requested subsidies for academic equipment should already have a considerable foundation, and it is hoped that there will be definite achievements after the subsidies are provided; (3) Schools that are temporarily approved to be established should not be subsidized in principle; (4) If the Ministry of Education believes that a certain special subject should be handled in a certain school due to national policy or local suitability, the original request may be changed, and subsidies for the special subject may be granted; (5) No subsidies will be granted for construction and recurring expenses; (6) The regional distribution of subsidies to schools should also be taken into consideration.

After the review standards were determined, the committee followed these standards, divided the process into two steps: approving the subsidy items and approving the subsidy amounts, and conducted a rigorous review. It was resolved that out of the total subsidy amount of 720,000 yuan, in addition to allocating 50,000 yuan for the Ministry of Education to reserve as temporary emergency relief funds for private colleges and universities this year, a total of 32 schools were approved for subsidies. The subsidy amounts for each school are as follows:

(1) Jinling University 30,000 yuan (2) Ginling College 12,000 yuan (3) Soochow University 10,000 yuan (4) Nantong College 35,000 yuan (5) Tatung University 35,000 yuan (6) Fudan University 15,000 yuan (7) Guanghua University 15,000 yuan (8) Great China University 15,000 yuan (9) University of Shanghai 20,000 yuan (10) Sino-French University Pharmaceutical College 10,000 yuan (11) Dongya Physical Education College 5,000 yuan (12) Suzhou Art College 6,000 yuan (13) Hangchow University 8,000 yuan (14) Xiamen University 90,000 yuan (15) Fukien Christian University 12,000 yuan (16) Hwa Nan College 8,000 yuan (17) Lingnan University 35,000 yuan (18) Guangzhou University 6,000 yuan (19) Guangdong National University 14,000 yuan (20) Guangdong Guanghua Medical College 8,000 yuan (21) West China Union University 20,000 yuan (22) Xiangya Medical College 35,000 yuan (23) Wuchang China University 8,000 yuan (24) Huachung University 15,000 yuan (25) Wuchang Boone Library School 5,000 yuan (26) Jiaozuo Institute of Technology 35,000 yuan (27) Shanxi Chuanzhi Medical College 15,000 yuan (28) Yenching University 60,000 yuan (29) Fu Jen Catholic University 10,000 yuan (30) Chaoyang University 8,000 yuan (31) Nankai University 40,000 yuan (32) Cheeloo University 30,000 yuan.

Among the above subsidy amounts for each school, Xiamen University and Yenching University have special economic circumstances and received more subsidies. After review by the Review Committee, it was decided that although Nankai University had already received subsidies from the National Treasury, it did not seem necessary to consider it again this time. However, because the school has always had excellent performance and has been engaged in research on applied sciences and practical problems, a subsidy was specifically granted to the project as an incentive. In addition, a small number of schools, although with relatively poor performance, did not fully meet the conditions set in the Outline of the Measures for the Distribution of Subsidies, but the committee granted subsidies to give these few schools the opportunity to strive for improvement. In addition, the subsidy amounts for some schools were specially and generously approved in consideration of their geographical location. In summary, among the 32 schools approved for subsidies, in terms of subject category, science, agriculture, engineering, and medicine accounted for 80.7 percent, and liberal arts, law, commerce, and education accounted for 19.3 percent. In terms of expense category, equipment costs accounted for 81.5 percent, and faculty costs accounted for 18.5 percent.

After reviewing the results of the Review Committee's report, the Ministry of Education considered that the subsidy amounts approved for each school were appropriate and submitted the original plan proposed by the Review Committee to the Executive Yuan for approval and filing, and requested that it be forwarded to the National Government for filing and promulgation. It is reported that this case was approved and filed by the Executive Yuan Conference the other day, but the timing of the promulgation will have to wait until the National Government has filed it in accordance with the regulations.

Measures for the Confucius Birthday Commemoration

The Ministry of Education issued a notice to the education bureaus of all provinces and cities on the 9th, stating that: "The Executive Yuan's Order No. 4166 states, 'The National Government's Order No. 502 states, 'For compliance, the Central Executive Committee's letter states, 'The 123rd Standing Committee of this committee has resolved to designate the birthday of Confucius as a national memorial day and has requested the government to promulgate it. The Propaganda Committee has also been asked to formulate memorial measures. The Central Propaganda Committee has consulted with the Ministry of Interior and the Ministry of Education to formulate memorial measures for the birthday of Confucius, with an attached order form for the memorial service. This has been submitted to and approved by the 122th Standing Committee of this committee with revisions. In addition to ordering it to be distributed to party departments at all levels, we are enclosing the case and the memorial measures and the order form for the memorial service for your reference. We hope that you will instruct your subordinates to comply and order the Ministry of Education to formulate a Confucius memorial song, etc.' This has been received and should be followed. In addition to replying to the letter and ordering the Executive Yuan to instruct the Ministry of Education to comply and distribute it, we are hereby copying and issuing the original attachments and ordering you to comply and instruct your subordinates to comply in the same way.' This has been received and should be followed. In addition to distributing it, we are hereby copying and issuing the original attachments and ordering you to comply and instruct your subordinates to comply in the same way.' This order."

The 128th Standing Committee of the Fourth Central Executive Committee passed the following measures for the Confucius Birthday Commemoration on July 5, 23rd year of the Republic: (1) Memorial Date: August 27th; (2) Name of the Memorial Day: Confucius Birthday Commemoration; (3) A Brief Biography of Confucius: Confucius, whose given name was Qiu and courtesy name was Zhongni, was a native of Lu. He aspired to learn in his youth, traveled widely in his prime, and expounded the way of Yao, Shun, Yu, Tang, Wen, Wu, and the Duke of Zhou to save the world and govern with benevolence and reciprocity. In his later years, he also deleted the Book of Poetry and the Book of Documents, established rites and music, praised the Book of Changes, and revised the Spring and Autumn Annals, leaving behind laws for future generations. He was the ancestor of Confucianism and was revered as a teacher and model by past dynasties. Sun Yat-sen, the Founding Father of the Republic of China, also praised him highly. Confucius was born in 1462 BC (the 21st year of King Ling of Zhou) and died in 1390 BC (the 41st year of King Jing of Zhou) at the age of 73; (4) Memorial Ceremony: A day off will be given on this day. All sectors of the country will hang flags to celebrate. Party, government, military, police, and school organs, as well as groups, will hold memorial meetings separately, and senior administrative organs in various places will convene memorial meetings for all sectors; (5) Key Points of Propaganda: 1. Explain Confucius's life story; 2. Explain Confucius's doctrines; 3. Explain the relationship between Sun Yat-sen's revolutionary thought and Confucius.

Attached: Order Form for the Confucius Birthday Commemoration Meeting (1) All stand at attention; (2) Play music; (3) Sing the Party song; (4) Bow three times to the Party and National flag, the portrait of the Premier, and the portrait of Confucius; (5) The chairman respectfully reads the Premier's will; (6) The chairman reports on the significance of commemorating Confucius; (7) Speech; (8) Sing the Confucius Memorial Song; (9) Play music (10) Ceremony concludes.

The front courtyard houses classrooms, an auditorium, a clinic, an exhibition room, a reception room, a library, etc., and the back courtyard houses dormitories, a dining room, a bathroom, and a lavatory. The purpose of our holding the Children's Health Camp is to train the children's physique and cultivate the children's knowledge. In the era of agricultural economy in China, most parents spun and weaved at home, and children could be educated and raised at any time. However, in today's era of industrial economy, parents in general families go out to work, and the family system is gradually collapsing, making it difficult to educate their children. If we do not seek remedies, the danger is extremely great. Therefore, the Summer Children's Health Camp is a way to remedy the lack of family education for children. I hope that all parents and people from all walks of life will enthusiastically support and promote it so that the facilities of this camp will be even more perfect next year. After the speech, the mayor personally gave gifts to the children.

Postponement of High School Entrance Examination

Postponed to August 20th

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau issued a notice on the postponement of the make-up examination for students who did not finish the examination due to illness during the second semester graduation examination for high school students in the 22nd academic year. The notice states that the bureau had previously scheduled a make-up examination for students who were unable to attend the examination or did not finish the examination due to illness or other reasons, and had issued a notice to that effect. As the date of the make-up examination is approaching, all students who are supposed to participate in this make-up examination have either not recovered from their illness or have left Shanghai to return to their hometowns, making it difficult for them to participate in the make-up examination as scheduled. Many have requested permission to postpone the examination. In consideration of the difficult circumstances of these students, the bureau has approved the postponement of the make-up examination to August 20th, 21st, and 22nd. The deadline for schools to submit the list and photos of students taking the make-up examination has been extended to the 14th of this month to facilitate the process. After this make-up examination, no further make-up examinations will be held for this academic year. All students must report on time and must not delay themselves. This notice is hereby issued for your information.

Chih Tze Middle School

Establishing Scholarship and Tuition Waiver Methods

Chih Tze Middle School on Water and Electricity Road, Zhabei, in order to encourage students' academic performance, the board of directors decided to establish 27 scholarship and tuition waiver positions starting from the autumn semester of this year. Students with good conduct and an average examination score of 80 or above, ranking first in their grade, will have their tuition, accommodation, and miscellaneous fees fully waived for the next semester. The second-ranked student will have all tuition fees waived, and the third-ranked student will have half of their tuition fees waived. There are nine positions for the three junior high school grades and 18 positions for the three senior high school general studies and business studies grades. Junior high school or senior high school graduates who meet the above conditions will be admitted to the senior high school or university freshman year with tuition waived. The school's enrollment is scheduled to take place on the 17th of this month, and the number of applicants has been quite enthusiastic recently.

Shen Bao Wireless Weekly

An Amateur-Style Transmitter

— Ying Fu

(Wavelength 40 to 100 Meters)

This transmitter is simple to manufacture, and the components are commonly used in radios. On the antenna side, no special installation is required. Friends who are interested in broadcasting may want to try it. However, during testing, the wavelength can only be within 40 to 100 meters. Of course, 200, 300, 600, or even 1000 meters are also possible. This only requires increasing the number of turns of the coils. However, these wavelengths are reserved for broadcasting. If amateur enthusiasts want to use wavelengths above 150 meters, then all radio reception within 25 kilometers will be disrupted. If the Ministry of Communications finds out, a lawsuit is inevitable. Therefore, it is best to test within 40 to 100 meters. Moreover, this type of wavelength can transmit far. I have used this machine for communication and reached a distance of 150 kilometers. It can transmit even further for telegraphy. At that time, the two tubes I used were Philips B405.

For the three coils, use No. 20 double silk-covered wire. On a three-inch diameter rubber tube, first wind Ll four turns, then leave about half an inch and wind four turns for L2. Do not break the wire. Continuously draw a wire end, about a quarter of an inch apart, and then wind four turns for L3.

In the ground circuit, connect an ammeter (0-1A5) or a small light bulb in series to see the oscillation situation.

For the high-frequency choke coil, use No. 30 double sand-covered wire and wind about 100 turns on a half-inch diameter and three-inch long wooden post.

If the wavelength used is 60 to 100 meters, then the number of turns of the above four coils must be increased by 50%.

T is the amplitude modulation transformer, with a ratio of 1:10 to 1:40. When not in use, use the switch S to short-circuit the microphone power supply. This dry battery is 4 to 9 volts.

AFC is a 30-henry low-frequency choke coil, which can be purchased ready-made.

To send a telegram, insert the telegraph key at X. This transmitter is inexpensive and lightweight and can be installed in a box for use as a travel transmitter. (End)

Using Ultra-Short Waves for Short-Range Communication

— Liu Tongkang

Holidays really give me a lot of convenience. Although the weather is so hot that people are sweating, it finally cannot stop my active heart.

In the past two weeks, the author has been experimenting with using ultra-short waves for short-range communication. As a result, the results can be considered satisfactory. Now I will briefly describe the experimental process for the reference of comrades.

Originally, experimenting with ultra-short waves was something we had longed for for a long time! After all, the result of hard work is that the seeds of hope have formed into the fruits of reality!

In an old Western publication, we actually found two circuits that suit our taste | | both economical and simple | | but because they cannot be used for both transmitting and receiving with one machine, and the equipment of parts requires doubling, we had to improve them. In this way, it not only conforms to the principle of economy, but also makes it more convenient to use and manage.

After the parts were assembled, the comparison test began. A total of two transceivers were assembled this time, so in fact no difficulties occurred! But the first communication test failed!

After a careful inspection, it was discovered that this was the case! It turned out that the vacuum tube I was using had been working for eight months, and the power of the filament to emit electrons would naturally be much weaker. When the screen voltage was low (22.5 volts), the vacuum tube did not oscillate! So I doubled the B voltage and then did the second test!

The test was successful in the early morning! This time we communicated with a distance of more than ten feet, and the wavelength was about five meters of ultra-short wave | | | It is a pity that the amplitude of the pronunciation is too narrow. If we did not use a slow-speed dial, this failure would be inevitable!

This experimental experience is really worth reporting to comrades. I hope comrades can also use ultra-short waves to conduct an experiment! And thoroughly research the ultra-short wave! This may be more meaningful than simply listening to broadcast music!

Application parts

C1 is a variable capacitor for adjusting the wavelength, with a capacity of 0.00005 MFD

C2 is a 0.000IMFD fixed capacitor

C3 is an OIMFD fixed capacitor

R1 is an I0000 ohm fixed resistor

J1 J2 are both closed jacks

V1 is a No. 30 power-saving vacuum tube.

T1 is an amplitude modulation transformer

M is a single-button microphone

L1 L2 are coils. If the wavelength is five meters, use a one-inch diameter rubber tube. L1 and L2 each wind two turns with 22-strand yarn-covered wire. A gap must be left between each turn to reduce losses. If the wavelength is 25 meters, L1 and L2 each wind six turns. The rest is the same.

When recording, insert the jack J1 at the X in Figure 2. When receiving, connect the headset to J2.

For other arrangements in the machine, it is better to keep the wiring short as shown in Figure 2. A slow-speed dial must be used for adjustment. Also, the front panel of the machine must be metal to avoid human induction.

Single-Tube AC/DC Dual-Purpose Radio Wang Maosheng

Ordinary AC radios require at least two vacuum tubes, one for rectification and one for detection. The 12A7 vacuum tube is a recent invention that combines rectification and detection into one tube, making it very convenient to use. Moreover, it can be used for both AC and DC power, and the efficiency is also high. Now I will introduce it as follows.

The 12A7 vacuum tube contains a pentode and a rectifier tube, with a total of seven pins. The grid is on top of the vacuum tube. The components shown on each pin are shown in the attached figure. The whole machine should be made of aluminum plates, about 5"X7" in size and about 2" high. A cover should be added to the vacuum tube to avoid noise. The ground wires shown in the figure can be gathered at a suitable point on the aluminum plate and connected to each other. Another 15"X7" Bakelite board is installed with SW, R4C2, J, etc. Other components are installed separately above or below the aluminum plate.

The ground wire can be grounded or not grounded at the Grd position. C1 depends on the height or length of the antenna.

The installation of this machine is simple and the operation is convenient. The capacity of each component is as shown in the figure.

Powerful Single-Tube Receiver with Crystal Detection

— KMK

The circuit diagram above is a modified version of one published in a certain wireless magazine. The effect of the experiment is very considerable and can be comparable to ordinary two-tube receivers. Using a speaker to play the broadcasts of local stations is loud enough, so I specially introduce it here for the enjoyment of interested readers. The circuit is named the Gernsback Megadyne type. It first uses a crystal for detection and then connects a powerful tube for amplification. The regeneration force is adjusted with a variable capacitor (C) and a variable resistor (R2) is used to control the tone. The coil L uses No. 30 enameled wire and is wound 75 turns on a three-inch diameter rubber tube. L uses No. 32 enameled wire and is wound 40 turns on a one-and-a-half-inch diameter rubber tube (installed in the middle of L so that it can rotate). R·F·C· can use No. 38 enameled wire and wind 252 turns on a three-quarter-inch diameter wooden shaft (with hard paper clamped at both ends of the shaft to prevent the wire from scattering). C is a .00025MF variable capacitor. C1 is a .0005MF variable capacitor. C2 is a .0005MF fixed capacitor. C3 is the same as C. R is a five megohm fixed resistor (i.e., 5MEG grid leak). RX is a twelve ohm variable filament resistor. R2 is a 10,000 ohm variable resistor. D·C· is a sensitive crystal (it is best to use a compound carbon type). The vacuum tube uses a No. 33 powerful pentode. A battery uses 1.5 volts or 3 volts (when using 3 volts, do not fully open the filament resistor, otherwise the filament may burn out). B battery uses 135 volts, but when using a headset, a B battery of 45 volts is enough.

Crystal Pocket Radio

— Jianqin

The pocket radio introduced now has been tested by several comrades, and the results are very remarkable. Its only advantage is that it is convenient to carry (the whole machine is installed in a single headset) and saves the trouble of adjustment. Without the need for antenna and ground wire installation, you can listen to beautiful music anytime and anywhere. The detailed manufacturing method is described below for the research of comrades.

Materials: Ordinary headset, one sensitive crystal, one thick cardboard, one small square of thin copper sheet, two yards of lamp wire, one connecting clip. Manufacturing method:

A is a stylus cut from a thin copper sheet. The dashed line indicates the curved position during installation.

B is a crystal cup, also made of copper sheet. Bend the four corners on the left and right to clamp the crystal. The three small holes at the top and bottom are empty to enter C.

C is cut from thick manure paper. Its surrounding size should be in tight contact with the inner wall of the headset. The size of the rectangular hole in the middle should be suitable for the two wire balls in the headset to pass through. The three small holes next to it are used to install the crystal cup.

D is the situation after installation. The dashed line indicates the wiring under the paper sheet.

E is the complete circuit diagram

How to receive the radio: In places near the broadcasting station, you only need to clip the clip to a wide range of metal objects. (For example, lead sheets, water tanks, lead sheaths of wires, iron beds, copper beds, metal supports, and metal chimneys, etc.) to receive beautiful music.

Note: When receiving radio, the iron rust or paint and all insulation materials must be scraped off from the place where the clip is clipped, and it is advisable to press the palm of your hand on the back of the headset, because there is a wire inside connected to the outer shell (that is, one end of the stylus and coil is connected to the magnet and the magnet is connected to the outer shell). Pressing your hand on it allows the current to enter the body. Because the human body has an electricity storage function, it can increase the volume. The dashed line F in Figure E indicates this meaning and does not mean that a ground wire is required.

Another Connection Method for Dual Speakers

— Lu Guizhen

Usually, when we connect dual speakers, we all use methods such as series connection or parallel connection. Now the author will introduce a new connection method, which was recently discovered. Although it is only limited to machines that are originally equipped with dynamic speakers! But it is very interesting. All comrades who have dynamic speakers on their radios can try it; people are not in danger of electric shock, and the speakers do not have to be directly connected to high-voltage electricity, so problems such as mismatched resistance, loss of magnetism, and broken wires can be avoided; the method is to connect one end of the speaker to the iron core of the original dynamic speaker of the machine, and connect the other end to the ground terminal.

Headphones can also be connected and used in the same way without any risk of damage.

Key Points for Selecting and Purchasing AC Radios (Continued)

— Jiang Zhiban

(3) Review of the structure Generally, low-priced imported AC radios often fail to be durable due to the desire to reduce costs. For example, filter capacitors are mostly made of low-value electrolytic or paste-type. This type of capacitor has a relatively low withstand voltage and a certain and relatively short lifespan. If the capacitor is broken down, the transformer and rectifier tube will also be damaged. According to the statistics of a large repair company, more than 75% of the diseases of radios are caused by the power supply, rectification, and filtering parts. Therefore, when purchasing a radio, it is best to have paper-based filter capacitors that can withstand high voltage, followed by carbon resistance resistors and volume controllers (i.e., variable carbon resistors). Poor design or manufacturing will cause a lot of noise a few weeks after purchasing the machine, and eventually damage, and burning out vacuum tubes and other components is also not uncommon. Carbon resistance resistors have a certain power consumption rate. In standardized designs, the power consumption rate of the carbon resistance resistor itself must be more than three times the actual power consumption rate. This will prevent overheating, changes in resistance, and damage, and can withstand long-term work. But in reality, the design is often very harsh, so it cannot be durable. As for the volume controller, it is often prone to noise and obstacles due to poor manufacturing, frequent rotation and friction. There are many other shortcomings. In short, if you are greedy for cheap and have no choice, you will not be fooled.

(4) Secrets of listening When purchasing a radio, you should first order the merchant to disassemble the internal machinery to see if the filter capacitor is made of paper, and whether the carbon resistance resistor has a large power consumption rate. Whether the construction of each part is solid and reliable. Then check the applied voltage and frequency numbers indicated on the trademark plate or power transformer to see if they meet the local power supply. If you are satisfied with everything, you can try listening. Listening is the only way to investigate a radio, and it also needs special attention. Do not let the merchant listen to several well-known radios, and think that you are satisfied. You must listen one by one according to the program list to see if there is any noise or interference. Whether the engraved index completely matches the frequency number of the radio station. You can also compare and listen to other brands of radios, so you will not make a mistake. Readers should pay attention to it.

Various Items

Idle Chatter on Wu Maidens

— Yan Qiao

For days, listening to the Suzhou Tan girls on "Lai Dian Hua," their singing voices are delicate and moving, truly soul-stirring. It suddenly reminded me of Bai Letian's poem: "Wu Maiden's Evening Rain Xiao Xiao Tune, long since I haven't heard it since leaving Jiangnan." Letian was, after all, a social poet, a man of many affections. Qian Mengsou has a line, "Who sings the Wu Maiden's Tune in the East Wind? Evening Rain Xiao Xiao surrounds the forbidden city." He also speaks of the Evening Rain Xiao Xiao Tune. Even Wang Yuyang has a poem saying, "Waves circle around Lei Pond in a stream, to this day the Shui Diao grieves Yangzhou, in recent years accustomed to hearing the Wu Maiden's Tune, Evening Rain Xiao Xiao above the water pavilion." "Seven years of farewell banquets, what can be done? Jade pot, red tears conceal green eyebrows, Evening Rain Xiao Xiao Nanyang Station, listening again to the Wu Maiden's Tune." Evening Rain Xiao Xiao, there probably really is such a tune. I wonder how it compares to today's drizzling rain?

Wu Maidens are not only good at singing; even those who don't sing have a reputation for beauty that is widely known. For example, the boat girls recorded in the "Wu Gate Pleasure Boat Records" were the object of Suzhou's amorous affections a hundred years ago. Later, Cangqiao Lane became Kai Pa Lane, and the boat girls fell out of fashion. However, some of the pleasure boats, those that row the boats, are still graceful and charming. Zeng Mengpu's "Flower in a Sinful Sea" has descriptions of these "hot water boats." They are called "hot water boats" because the boats are rowed so slowly that the water is stirred up and becomes warm. But now it's not the same. Although a few pleasure boats can still be found near Guangji Bridge, the boat girls are all wrinkled and old. Which young girl would still patiently stay on these cold water boats?

Matchmakers are also a type of Wu Maiden, having cultivated a mouth that can speak a torrent of flowery words. If you listen from across the wall, no one can tell if they are young or old, but their voices are always soft, gentle, and melodious. They rely on a few old rules and the traditional family customs of the ladies and grandmothers, and can still pass down their profession through generations, occupying a position in weddings, funerals, and celebrations. But many families are also doing away with them.

In the past, Suzhou women liked to be particular about their hairstyles. If they felt their own skills were lacking, they would hire someone to do their hair, and thus a type of "hairdresser aunt" was created. It is likely that people who made a living this way could not be too old. They freely entered people's homes, and could talk about anything with their female clients. In the past, they were certainly considered outstanding in their profession. However, since the fashion of short hair became popular, their business has greatly declined.

The latter two types of women have become a waning force in Suzhou society. Therefore, Wu Maidens as Wu Maidens have become haggard and pathetic.

As for the singing Wu Maidens, they are also in decline. Although old brothels can still be found that offer wine and shave heads, they cannot openly send notes or respond to calls, and they are also silent and do not sing at banquets. So, the Evening Rain Xiao Xiao Tune is almost impossible to hear in Suzhou. Only female storytellers sing a few popular tunes when they are in good spirits. But most likely, those who listen to the songs have other intentions. So, isn't the Wu Maiden's Song about to become a thing of the past?

Idle Talk of Suzhou

— Shi Jiu

The city of Suzhou is in the shape of a turtle, and in the past, it only had six city gates. This symbolizes the turtle's head, tail, and four feet. It is said that at the end of the Yuan dynasty, Xu Da besieged Zhang Shicheng in Suzhou for a long time, and after nine months, he still could not conquer it. Someone offered a plan, saying, "The city of Suzhou is in the shape of a turtle. Attacking all six points simultaneously will only make it stronger. It is better to choose one point to attack quickly, which may break it." At that time, it so happened that Shicheng had a trusted confidant named Li Situ, who secretly sent someone to Xu Da's army to surrender. Thus, Xu Da was able to attack through Changmen and enter the city.

Changmen has always been known as prosperous, while Fengmen is extremely desolate. Being the same city gate, why is there such a difference? There is a small anecdote behind this: After Xu Da attacked through Changmen and entered the city, he did not kill a single person, and was hailed as a benevolent and righteous army. At that time, Chang Yuchun was annoyed that the city had not been broken for so long, and he attacked through Fengmen, sparing even three-year-old children. Although Xu Da hurriedly sent someone with a token to stop him, the Fengmen area had already suffered the pain of bloodshed. Therefore, Fengmen is uniquely desolate, while Changmen is extremely prosperous, and it is still like this today.

Even today, the people of Suzhou still have lingering thoughts of Zhang Shicheng, a native of Suzhou. On the thirtieth day of the seventh lunar month, every household burns Nine Thoughts Incense, which is to commemorate his kindness and virtue. When Suzhou was not defended and about to fall, Shicheng's mother said to him, "My son, you have failed. What about my words?" Shicheng then drove all his relatives up to Qiyun Tower and set it on fire. He alone did not die, saying, "I am saving the lives of the people in the city." Then, he surrendered himself. This is a great tragedy in the local history of Suzhou.

Suzhou was anciently known as "Gusu." According to historical records, Gusu was originally Guxu, and both the terrace and the mountain were named after Wu Zixu. In the Wu dialect, "Xu" is mistakenly pronounced as "Su," hence the name "Gusu." Another theory is that after the state of Wu was destroyed, Gusu Terrace was also abandoned, and only Xu Mountain remained. Therefore, it was called "Gu Xu." Later, "Xu" was mistakenly pronounced as "Su," and "Gu" was mistaken for "Gu," hence the name "Gusu."

The dry city gate of Fengmen was once renamed "Little East Gate" during the Taiping Heavenly Kingdom era. The original stone drawbridge was also dismantled at that time. Gunboats were stationed in the city river to provide defense. There is a small典故about Suzhou having a Little East Gate. In another twenty or thirty years, I am afraid no one will know about it, so I am recording it.

The Nighttime West Lake in Hangzhou

— Bai Ying

In Hangzhou, the nighttime West Lake becomes bustling due to the hot summer.

Especially on the eighteenth day of the sixth lunar month.

The eighteenth day of the sixth lunar month is the birthday of Guan Yin, the Goddess of Mercy. Therefore, old ladies must chant their prayers, and West Lake must, as usual, have a night of lotus lanterns!

According to the elderly, in the Qing dynasty, all three city gates would be opened all night long, and officials from the provincial governor and down would have to tour the lake and celebrate until dawn, just like ordinary people!

Naturally, this year it cannot be called off due to droughts and floods. Qianyi Commercial Building had already bought the finest fireworks from Huizhou for a thousand yuan to add to the excitement of West Lake on the eighteenth day of the sixth lunar month. It was published in the newspaper, and people were stirred up like a tidal wave.

Thus, this year's West Lake night on the eighteenth day of the sixth lunar month is even more lively and vibrant!

I was also pulled along by a friend to make up the numbers.

We entered the Sixth Park on the lakeside around 9:30. However, the tourists at this time were already as dense as white ants, stepping on each other's heels. The unpleasant scent of powder mixed with sweat filled the air, making one feel nauseous.

I heard that the fireworks would be launched at ten o'clock. As the time approached, it suddenly started to rain. The people in the park were instantly in chaos, pushing and shoving towards the gate. Some of the bolder ones still lay on the grass, leisurely watching the dark clouds in the sky, some round and some square.

The rain became lighter. The firework架子called "Fa Bao," which cost a thousand yuan and was erected on the water, was very high. One by one, snakelike Huizhou fireworks shot straight into the sky, fiery red!

"Oh, the fireworks are here! The fireworks are here!"

In the midst of this cheering, many tourists re-entered the gate. The lakeside park was once again crowded!

The sky was clear, and the moon brought coolness to the sky. West Lake was even more beautiful! Red lights flickered around the lake, and the ripples were so interesting!

Several silver bell-like singing voices floated from the surface of the lake, engraved in everyone's hearts.

Ah, here there is no drought! No flood!

Secret That Flew Here

— Shi Cheng

The scenery of West Lake is elegant and refined, unparalleled in its ordinariness; whether lightly adorned or heavily painted, it is always suitable. I once ascended the Chuyang Terrace, overlooking the entire West Lake; the dikes draped with green willows, the waves reflecting the mountain light, Buddhist temples hidden in the verdant peaks, the sound of bells occasionally heard from the monasteries, it was as if one had entered a painting, no longer having the atmosphere of worldly life! It is said that among the scenic spots around the lake, Yunlin is the most outstanding; the Lingyin Flying Peak, in particular, is full of strange rocks and wondrous peaks! These words, I quite agree with.

A Line of Sky is at the foot of the Flying Peak, where the rock crevice is as thin as a line, faintly protecting the light of the sky. Looking up, Buddhist images appear in the middle, some ugly, some beautiful, some golden, some red; what each traveler sees is different. Virtuous men and believing women then say that our Buddha is spiritual, revealing this sacred迹象; the incense in the Buddhist temples greatly increases as a result. Little do they know that to see the Tathagata through form and appearance is already a violation of the Buddhist commandment of walking the evil path. Yet the monks still widely promote this to deceive the common people. Alas, the depth of superstition among people is profound!

Master Jizhao is my friend. He is outstanding and refined, free and unrestrained from the mundane world. Once, on a moonlit night, he and I answered the invitation of Yao Ziyuan and drank at his residence. Yao Zi is fond of cultivating flowers. Ascending his terrace, it was like entering a land of fragrant flowers. Sipping wine under the moon was especially interesting. We had a leisurely conversation, enjoying ourselves and forgetting fatigue. When we were halfway through the wine, I casually asked him about it. The master rolled his eyes and said, "This is just a deceiving trick. Why are you so confused by it?" I laughed and thanked him, and asked him for the reason. The master said: "The peaks and rocks are exquisite, with many holes. The monks choose the larger ones and place windmills inside. Buddhist images are molded on all eight sides, with different clothing and colors. When the wind comes through the rock crevice, it spins continuously. Looking up from below, one can only see a line, so the Buddhist image reflected in the eyes changes with time. If one were to climb to the top of the peak and look down through the rock crevice, the true appearance would be revealed. As years pass, those who know the truth become few, and they are surprised to believe it is a divine phenomenon. Isn't that confusing?" Yao Zi said: "The technique is indeed ingenious! Aren't you afraid that tourists will discover the truth?" The master said: "There are too many rock crevices, making it difficult to find them. Moreover, the top of the peak is covered with thorns, which is enough to hinder the feet of tourists." These were the master's words. Is it a Zhuangzi allegory? Or is it something he actually saw? It cannot be known. I will record it and wait for future verification.

Suzhou Sketches

— Wei Ji

Suzhou, called the paradise of Suzhou. I think everyone is envious of the people living in Suzhou.

Suzhou, called paradise in the past, truly deserved the name. But now, Suzhou has also suffered from unemployment panic and economic bankruptcy. It is no longer as enviable as before.

Now I will talk about the Suzhou of today.

Guanqian Street, the most prosperous street in paradise. Now it is covered with banners advertising big discounts. Every store uses radio to broadcast beautiful music and humorous talks, hoping to attract pedestrians to stop, but business is still slow.

In the cinemas, first-class films are being shown at the lowest prices. But the place is still deserted, with few spectators.

In the job centers, there are many women from the countryside. Their husbands have been affected by the economic bankruptcy in the countryside, and they have been told to come to the city to make a living.

On Jinchang Road, there are many women lined up next to the hotels every night, selling their bodies and looking for their customers for the night.

In short, paradise has felt the recession, and perhaps it will turn into hell in the future!

Nighttime Congee Shops in Hangzhou

— Jin Xi

The Yanling Road area in Hangzhou is the concentration point for nighttime congee shops. The nighttime congee shops on this street all employ young female attendants. The old bosses of the congee shops use the charm and smiles of women to attract customers and expand their business. By analogy, the nature of Hangzhou's nighttime congee shops is similar to that of Shanghai's Jiafei 座 (a type of bar).

Although they are called congee shops, in terms of their business scope, they are actually a disguised form of restaurant. Those young and beautiful female attendants are the most capable people in the shop to promote wine and dishes. Relying solely on a few bowls of congee and a few plates of side dishes, the bosses' profits are minimal. They rely entirely on the female attendants' attentive service to those customers who are slightly色躁 (sexually restless). They have a kind of charm that is enough to urge customers to order a few side dishes that they do not necessarily need, and the price of these side dishes is so expensive.

Those who frequent nighttime congee shops are mostly car drivers, store clerks, retired military police, and perhaps a few wealthy people, gentlemen, adults, painters, and government officials, but these are in the minority. The working hours of nighttime congee shop female attendants start at one o'clock in the afternoon and end at twelve o'clock at night. From one o'clock to seven o'clock in the afternoon, there are very few customers who are willing to spend money. When night falls and the electric lights are brilliant, customers of all sorts gather in the nighttime congee shop to drink, order dishes, wave their fists, tease the female attendants, and act out all kinds of ugly scenes. When the wine is drunk and the ears are hot, the customers' hands will travel over every part of the female attendants' bodies. They will not refuse, they know that the customers are coming for this benefit.

In an unreasonable society, there is no reasonable life. From this alone, one can know how low the personality of Hangzhou poor women is in their profession.

Women Carrying Sedan Chairs Under Mount Tianping in Suzhou

— Zhu Weiming

Before the boat reached the foot of Mount Tianping, two or three strong women emerged from the thatched cottages under the green shade on the opposite shore. As soon as they saw the boat docking by the stone bridge, they jumped and ran to the shore, vying to say, "Do you want a sedan chair? Take a sedan chair up the mountain!" The soft and gentle Wu dialect sounds more pleasing than jazz music.

I stood on the bow of the boat, the duckweed leaning against my shoulder, and said to them with a smile, "We do want a sedan chair, but we need to eat before we go up the mountain." They knew that their hopes would not be dashed, so they all laughed and said, "Oh! Then we will go eat too." They all twisted their嬌軀 (pretty bodies) and ran away lightly, disappearing behind the green shadows. When we had barely finished half of our lunch, a young woman in her twenties had already returned to the shore to wait. She quietly sat on a white stone protruding from the water, her dark and large eyes, full and strong waist, revealed a small mouth staring at us. After a while, she suddenly smiled, and then splashed the blue-green waves with her palms, her figure reflected in the waves, trembling with the gurgling ripples.

We hired a total of four sedan chairs to go up the mountain. Women accounted for six of the sedan chair carriers. They were equally strong and had the same beautiful faces. They were also very young, only seventeen or eighteen to twenty years old. Two of them were young girls, the rosy clouds on their peach blossom cheeks showing that they were in their most moving and lovable time, but the burden of life had already been placed on their shoulders. 牛馬般的(Isn't carrying a sedan chair an inhuman life?) Labor drove them to struggle on the road of life. The other two men were a pair of captives from the city of smoke. They were exhausted, weak, and wretched. From their words and titles, it sounded like this pair of smokers were the husbands of the two young women inside.

After crossing two hills, about ten miles, we sat comfortably in the sedan chairs and already felt a little tired from the bumps. The pair of smokers were of course completely useless and exhausted. But the six women were always flying on foot. But the sweat had already rolled down from their foreheads to their mouths like a tide, soaking their necks and backs, seeping into their clothes and pants, and their whole bodies were as if they had taken a bath, emitting a vigorous heat. They immediately took off their coats, leaving only a short shirt, their full breasts抖抖地 (shaking), as if they were about to jump out of their shirts. A young woman carrying me was wiping the sweat hanging straight down her face with one hand, and rolling up her trouser legs with the other. "Ah! The sweat has soaked the color off my pants, look at how messy my thighs are!" It turned out that she was wearing blue cloth pants, and she rolled up her trouser legs high, her thighs fully exposed, and she just laughed foolishly, raising her face.

The women carrying sedan chairs on Mount Tianping are highly praised by tourists, and I think this must include the relationship of the labor union environment. So I took this opportunity to ask them in detail about their living conditions. According to them, because there are many mountains nearby, the productivity of the land is weak, and the mountain fields are worthless. There is also nothing produced on the mountains, so the men have nothing to do and sit in tea houses all day long chatting, and most of them are addicted to opium and red pills. The only work they can find is to open mountains and dig stones for people. However, none of the men who work as mountain openers do not eat opium or swallow red pills. Their wages are one yuan for three days, but their opium consumption, one yuan is only enough for two days. So not only their food, clothing, and housing expenses, but also their opium, must be forced to be provided by their wives, who are made to work like cattle and horses, and their wives' blood and sweat must be exhausted to swallow it. In addition to carrying sedan chairs, women also engage in embroidery as a side business, which is almost their inherited skill, and they embroider figures, flowers, and birds with extraordinary exquisiteness. The Gu Embroidery sold in the Shanghai market is actually all their production. Gu Embroidery shops send people to the countryside to deliver the work to be done to them, agree on a time to collect it, and the wages are extremely low, usually only two or three hundred 文 (cash) a day. Therefore, as soon as they see tourists going up the mountain, they rush to carry sedan chairs, although it is hard work, at least they can always earn a few毛 (cents).

The ladies who return from touring Mount Tianping only hear them praise the women carrying sedan chairs for their beauty and strength, or at most feel a little surprised. How do they know that their actual lives are so painful! Those who pay attention to women's issues can refer to it.

Commercial News

U.S. to Nationalize Silver

Gold Market Presents a Chaotic Situation

Deferred Delivery Premium Rises, Major Short Sellers Anxious About Recovery to One Yuan

Yesterday, the gold market was in a state of chaos due to the US government's announcement that it would nationalize silver. There was a potential short squeeze, and prices were extremely firm after a period of weakness. In the morning, the overseas silver market, both in the UK and the US, saw a sharp rise. The forward silver price on the Five Metals Exchange, due to the government announcement, was set at US$0.5001 per ounce, with all months priced at US$0.4996, an increase of between 0.011 and 0.096. London spot gold rose by half a penny, and exchange rates also rose significantly. US cotton rose 19 points, and US wheat rose 1.5 cents. Market sentiment remained cautious. However, some believed that with the US government's silver nationalization price set at US$0.5001, the US silver price would be fixed around US$0.50, lacking the potential for a sharp rise. Therefore, off-exchange trading was extremely chaotic. Raw material prices initially rose strongly from 49 yuan, then retreated to 41 yuan, before recovering. Gold firms' preliminary trading started at 43.4 yuan and gradually rose. After opening, banks' appetite was unstable, both buying near-term and selling far-term. Although sentiment was positive, prices only fluctuated, with intense struggles. The Hongkong and Shanghai Banking Corporation (HSBC) announced its exchange rates, with the British pound up 1.25 and the US dollar up 0.5 yuan. The domestic market loosened. Reuters reported from New York that after the government's silver nationalization, there would be measures such as increasing silver certificates, creating silver coins, and increasing the silver reserve ratio to 3:1. New York Stock Market Enthusiastically Trending Upward

According to a report from Sin Feng Trading Company, yesterday (the 9th), the New York Stock Exchange, small exchanges, and commodity markets all surged vigorously. This was because silver was nationalized, which was generally seen as a precursor to inflation. President Roosevelt had previously delivered a speech favoring short positions, but the sound of his words was still in our ears when he took the swift action of nationalizing silver. This was truly beyond the expectations of Wall Street figures. When the news arrived, speculators were shocked and couldn't stop. Within an hour before the market closed, a strong buying trend developed on the exchange. The ticker tape lagged behind the market by as much as three minutes. All stocks rose in unison, with silver stocks and stocks benefiting from inflation being particularly strong. The surge reached around five dollars. At the same time, the bond market also became the focus of speculators' attention. The lively atmosphere evoked memories of the days of the Great War. Total trading volume for the day reached 21.76 million yuan, but transactions in the final hour alone reached 14.6 million yuan. As Wall Street studied and interpreted the situation, prices also rose and fell rapidly, creating exceptional confusion. Once it was recognized as inflationary, it immediately declined sharply, only showing improvement before the close. Some believed this was due to government intervention behind the scenes. U.S. government bonds initially rose slightly, but the results were mixed. The U.S. dollar fell sharply due to selling from Europe, also attributed to inflation as silver prices stabilized. Grains reached new highs due to the heat in the Midwest. Total trading volume for the day was 1.42 million shares. The Dow Jones New York indices are listed below:

Cotton Yarn: Both Bulls and Bears Hesitant and Uneasy

Complex Process of Cotton Yarn

The yarn market's situation changed three times a day, becoming increasingly complex. Both bulls and bears were in a state of frantic disarray, demonstrating the unsettled minds of speculators. When prices rose, buyers went wild; when news was bad, sellers were numerous. However, it was found that factories hedged a significant amount in recent days. Today, the market situation appeared slightly calmer, not as intense as the previous day.

Golden Rooster Hesitates, Slight Increase

The standard yarn market opened in the morning, with U.S. cotton rising again. Although factories had hedged the previous day, the decline was too severe, leading to profit-taking. Yesterday, the market turned upward. Front-month contracts rose by 0.67 to 1.23 yuan. In the second session, market prices suddenly changed, as factories hedged again, and selling pressure rose again. Contracts for all months suddenly fell by 0.89 yuan to 1 yuan. The third session remained weak. It was heard that spot yarn sales were still good, and contracts for all months rebounded by 0.67 yuan. As a result, contracts for all months rose by 0.1, 0.3, 0.5, and 0.6 yuan. The total trading volume was 43,900 bales.
