Shen Bao Local Supplement

Essays

"Beauties" and "Talents"

— Wang Ren

An era inevitably produces a special kind of person; this is a certain principle. Since ancient times, China has had emperors in every dynasty, with many heroes and famous scholars assisting them. At the same time, many ornamental figures are also produced: such as so-called beauties and talents. Opening any ancient book, one can always find records of their deeds.

Naturally, under the solid walls of feudalism and etiquette in the past, there were also special figures such as so-called filial sons and obedient grandsons, and even more common were women who valued their chastity like jade, earning them memorial arches for their virtuousness!

However, the era has changed now. It is no longer an era of producing loyal ministers, filial sons, or chaste and heroic women. What remains for us today that leaves a lasting impression are only the talents and beauties. However, these talents and beauties are not like the polite and dignified figures of the past, or the suave and elegant ones, who were called talents and beauties. Nor are they like those who spent their years deep in their boudoirs, cultivating fair skin, writing poems, making embroidery, and playing the zither, before they could be worthy of such praise. Today's talents must have the heroic essence attached to their literary air, and they must have expertise: such as poets, novelists, artists... only then can they be worthy of being different and becoming a successful talent in society. Otherwise, among the masses, the reputation of a talent cannot be appropriated by you. The same goes for beauties. Moreover, today's beauties must not be weak and reclusive, or be able to write poetry and calligraphy. They must be capable of fulfilling their duties happily. Like men, they should go out and participate in activities. In vast groups and among the masses, they must seize a worthy and praiseworthy reputation, such as social butterflies, empresses, and so on. Otherwise, the reputation of a beauty will not come to your head, and you will forever be just an insignificant figure!

Therefore, today's talents and beauties no longer hold the same prestigious position in society as in the past, and the ways to achieve it are greatly different.

We can now cite two men and women who are most prominent at present, and it is okay to praise them as talents and beauties!

One is the young aviator Sun Tonggang, who returned to the country from Germany a few months ago. When he was studying in Germany, of course, no one knew him. But once he rose up, as the saying goes, "If he doesn't fly, he's fine; but once he flies, he'll amaze the world." In less than two months, he became famous throughout the country. Although he has his own special skills, it is not inappropriate for us to praise him as a talent of the times.

The other is Miss Yang Xiuqiong, the so-called "mermaid," who is now making a big splash. After the National Games, she revealed her reputation, and then won the victory in the Far East Games, and was praised as "Miss China." Within a few months, she rose rapidly, and today, she has almost the magical power to captivate the masses. Almost everyone in the entire society is crazy about her. A certain committee member is willing to lower himself to hold her whip, and other celebrities and wealthy merchants cannot help but bow down before her pomegranate skirt. Some young men and women simply drool with deep envy! [Statement: This is not the author insulting Ms. Yang or making any jokes. The enthusiastic welcome of Ms. Yang in various places in recent days can prove it!] Therefore, with her fame throughout the country and great success, Ms. Yang is of course more than worthy of receiving the praise of a beauty; she should be the beauty among beauties.

We admire talents and beauties of the Sun Tonggang and Yang Xiuqiong type, and we do not want to see talents and beauties like those of the past who only played with words and painted their faces. However, while we hope, we deeply hope that successful talents and beauties do not use their success solely as a tool for showing off, or only become ornaments of society, like the talents and beauties of the past. We hope that all talents and beauties can make genuine contributions to the country and practical rewards to society with their knowledge and skills, instead of merely receiving beautiful names and becoming playthings and entertainment for the general public!

Philosophy of Man

— Xi Zhen

I always felt that the phrase "One dollar per ticket, everyone can get one" in the aviation lottery advertisements was a bit logically flawed. The phrase "everyone can get one" is untenable, because "people who can't come up with a dollar can't get one." I often thought that.

However, one day while walking on the street, I saw a crowd gathered in front of a small restaurant. I squeezed in to see what was happening: the large owner was twisting a young man's arm, demanding money, saying that he owed more than a dollar in total, and hadn't paid for more than a month. "If you can't even come up with a dollar, can you still be considered a person? I'd rather not have it, leave that coat behind, and get out!" Then there was a slap in the face.

"Can someone who can't even come up with a dollar still be considered a person?" The philosopher contemplated that sentence, thinking about the phrase "One dollar per ticket, everyone can get one," and then jumped up with joy as if a mathematician had solved a difficult problem. I understand, I understand! I suddenly understood it all!

"People who can't come up with a dollar were originally not considered people at all, so isn't this 'everyone can get one' absolutely true?"

Contemplating these eight words, they are a clear snapshot of current society. I memorized them as literary and philosophical treasures. You can't find such phrases in Plato's dialogues.

For example, if humans are different from other animals (that is, beasts), then in the current social environment, it is because humans have money, while other animals do not. Even the stubborn gorilla king Kong in the movies knows how to love women, but it doesn't know how to love Yuan Shikai. This point shows the excellence of humans in the animal kingdom. Thus, as the aviation lottery advertisements implicitly state, and the scene in front of the small restaurant shows, just one dollar serves as the dividing line between humans and other animals: "If you have a dollar, you are a person; if you don't have a dollar, you can't be considered a person."

I remembered that Lao Ciji had once answered the question, "Why are humans different from other animals?" In his answer, he attempted to explain the difference between humans and other animals in terms of labor methods. His conclusion was: humans can create and use production machinery; other animals (even apes and gorillas) cannot. If we must use Lao Ciji's words to explain the small restaurant owner's opinion, it is not absolutely impossible: isn't "money" the modern production machinery? Those who have gone hungry can understand this intuitively without much thought.

But unfortunately, if humans really use "money" as the dividing line between themselves and other animals, it is not a clever thing to do. If that's the case, what can humans still be proud of in the animal kingdom? Once other animals acquire the ability to "manufacture production machinery," wouldn't they also be able to become like humans? Let's use an example to illustrate this: "In modern times, people without money live inhuman lives." This statement probably won't be denied, right? But if we think about the deceased dog star Rin Tin Tin, it can use its own services to exchange for money just like humans. It can create "production machinery" and give it to people; thus, it lives a comfortable life as a wealthy person, enjoying the superior status of the "upper class."

We often hear people say: "The world is really messed up now. People with money are people; people without money are animals." Turning it around, we see: "People without money are animals, and animals with money are also people."

Previously, we said that "money" was only the dividing line between humans and other animals, but now "money" has further become the "admission ticket" to humanity. "Human area, no admittance to idlers": but those with admission tickets are not subject to this rule.

I would like to think that this is a myth, an absurd legend; but the facts are clearly placed before us, and we cannot deny them. I once saw a philosopher write a sentence in his book: "Humans are not a clever animal." At least, when it comes to the craze for "money," we cannot help but believe it.

But because everyone needs to have money to eat, even I have to become a "not very clever animal." However, I have since lost the pride of being human. That's right: "Humans are not a clever animal."

In a "not very clever" state, let us work hard to obtain the "admission ticket to humanity" forever.

Notes

Four Disagreement Principles of Guangdong Province

— A Feng

After the Guangdong provincial authorities strictly prohibited men and women from traveling together, the Guangdong Political Research Association further passed five items regarding gender boundaries: (1) prohibiting men and women from riding in the same vehicle, (2) prohibiting men and women from eating together, (3) prohibiting men and women from living together, (4) prohibiting military personnel from walking with civilians, (5) cinemas are prohibited from screening films co-starring men and women. Among the above five items, except for the fourth item, which is an exception regarding "togetherness," most are prohibitions on joint behaviors between men and women. Roughly speaking, they prohibit men and women from swimming together, walking together, eating together, and living together, which can be called the Four Disagreement Principles.

Gambling is open in Guangdong Province, and smoking is open. The authorities fully allow people their freedom and do not prohibit them, but they are particularly strict about the relationship between men and women, perhaps even more so than the rules of the Duke of Zhou. What does this mean? It is truly prohibiting what should not be prohibited, and not prohibiting what should be prohibited. Such a "reversal" policy is laughable. I have playfully composed two bamboo branch poems and recorded them below:

First Poem

The great defense between men and women is decreed, swimming, walking, living, and eating cannot be done together.

There are other paradises for roaming and reveling, all in the opium dens and gambling dens.

Second Poem

Heavy taxes and miscellaneous levies weigh down, smoking and gambling are taxed especially fiercely.

The most disastrous place for young people, mandarin ducks are split and do not meet!

Suzhou's Little Confusion

I have been to Suzhou, visited Xuanmiao Temple, and heard Little Confusion chatter nonsensically, which was very interesting. He said that people are born wrong; eyebrows should grow on fingers, which can be used as toothbrushes; the nose should be turned upside down so that a Parker or Conklin fountain pen can be inserted; one eye should grow in the front and one in the back so that one can take care of both front and back; and the anus should grow on the top of the head so that an umbrella can be inserted on rainy days. This kind of talk is truly imaginative, and the audience opened their mouths and laughed at him.

As a result, he sold hundreds of pieces of herbal pear syrup candy. Alas!

One Day

— Meng Jun

Waking up in the morning, the pale yellow sunlight was already shining obliquely on the head of the bed, dazzling my eyes. Even if I wanted to turn over and take another nap, I was afraid I couldn't sleep soundly anymore. I got up, took some cold water from the lead kettle, rinsed my mouth, and washed my face. I looked at the clock; it was already half past seven.

At this time, my mother also got up. She asked me what I wanted to eat? Should she ask A Jin to buy it? Every morning my mother asks me this, but I always just quickly make some cold rice with boiling water because of the time constraints, and consider it a breakfast. To me, this is nothing, but my mother always stares at me, as if to say, "Is it too bland?"

After I got dressed, I looked back at the clock just before leaving. Another fifteen minutes had passed unceremoniously; it was a quarter to eight. Walking out the door, I calculated in my mind that if there were no delays on the road, I could still make it to the factory before half past eight. Although being ten minutes or fifteen minutes late wouldn't really matter, why should I have to see their faces? I walked to the tram stop, and luckily the tram arrived.

After getting off the tram, I transferred to a public bus. I saw the big clock opposite the Great World pointing to eight o'clock. When getting on the public bus at this time, I always saw some familiar faces that I encountered every day. Everyone mechanically sat down, smoked, or looked out the window.

The so-called "going to the office" happens at this time.

The bus arrived at Sichuan Road, and a group of people got off. The Bund, another group got off. Nanjing Road, Beijing Road, groups of people got off. After passing Beijing Road, there were only a few people left on the bus. "Those who eat foreign company meals," Shanghai has a unique abundance of this kind of talent! A sentence I will never forget floated into my mind again: "In Shanghai, it is not easy to recruit a hundred dogs, but to recruit a hundred Chinese who can speak English can be done immediately."

The education in a semi-colonial country is remarkably successful, which cannot help but make me sad.

The bus arrived at its destination at only five minutes before eight thirty. I got off the bus, walked into the factory building, and the clattering of the machines came to my ears. Everything at the factory was as usual. I stepped into the door, and the gatekeeper always said, "Mr. X, good morning," sometimes adding, "Hot today, isn't it?" My response was just a nod or a "hm."

The desk was piled with nothing but letters and bills. Two or three foremen were waiting at the office window for the key to get materials. Dealing with this and busying with that occupied the whole morning, without even five minutes to spare for a quick smoke.

Time always flies faster when people are busy with this and that. The three and a half hours of the morning passed in an instant. Then, whoosh! The whistle blew, it was lunchtime. The factory does not provide lunch, so I had to go to a restaurant to eat. I often had a bowl of mixed soup and two bowls of white rice, which was considered the second meal of the day. This bowl of mixed soup truly lived up to its name, with greens, vermicelli, meat skin, tofu skin, edamame, and some other things I couldn't name all mixed together in a big bowl. A first-class meal cost no more than 360 to 500 wen in total.

In the afternoon, from one o'clock, it was back to office work until five o'clock. As long as the workers hadn't left, there wouldn't be a moment to spare. Today was even more exceptional. The work assigned for the day was not finished by five o'clock. Writing this, copying that, quietly, except for the gatekeeper, I was the only one left in the factory. If I wanted to complain about my fate, I couldn't really complain so much. Just the fact that workers could record overtime and get extra pay was enough to make me sigh with inferiority.

Leaving the factory, I threw my tired body onto the public bus, and sat down simply not wanting to move anymore. Even if there were one or two brightly dressed women sitting next to or opposite us on the bus, they couldn't raise my drooping eyes.

When the bus arrived at the Great World, I subconsciously raised my eyes and looked at the big clock opposite, which was pointing exactly at seven o'clock.

Amateur Mailbox

Unpaid Rent

— Editor

To the Esteemed Editor:

I really find it a bit difficult to say, and I'm very embarrassed to tell you about this, but circumstances are pressing me, forcing me to seek your advice.

I rented a room on North Sichuan Road, and recently, due to unemployment, I owe three months' rent. Two months ago, the landlord repeatedly urged me to pay, or he would rather sacrifice a month's rent and ask me to move out. Sir, when a person is poor, his ambitions are short-lived. I can barely afford to eat, so where would I get the money to pay rent? Friends and family, seeing how poor I am, are unwilling to let me stay with them. Therefore, I deceived him, saying that money would definitely be sent home next month, and if I didn't pay next month, he could seize my belongings. But to this day, things remain the same, and I have no solution. So, the landlord, on the one hand, drove me to despair

Page 19

and on the other hand, seized all my belongings. Fortunately, a friend, remembering our friendship, allowed me to stay, so I wouldn't be left homeless. But daily necessities must be provided by myself, so I went to the landlord to ask for my washbasin and towel. Unexpectedly, the landlord insisted on not returning them until I paid in full. I said, my bed alone is enough to cover the rent owed. What reason do you have to seize all my belongings? But he wouldn't reason with me, and I have no way to deal with it. May I ask, sir, do I have the right to take back my daily necessities? What method should I use to deal with him? I earnestly seek your guidance. With respectful wishes,

Yours sincerely, Li Yunsheng bowing

Answer: If you fail to pay rent, the landlord not only has the right to retain your belongings but also can obtain compensation or sell the retained items without having to petition the court. The right of retention can be auctioned off according to the method of pledge. However, the things retained also have a considerable range. The retained items only need to be sufficient to pay the rent owed, and the tenant can take back the remaining items. If the value of your bed is enough to cover the rent, then the remaining items can naturally be taken back. If he refuses to reason with you, you can turn to the leasing regulations in the Continued Compilation of Civil Law and show them to him. That way, he will naturally have nothing to say.

Fiction

The Simpleton (4)

— Lin Bin

Hunger turned the simpleton into a long-term worker who ate for free without pay. During the day, his stomach didn't rumble as badly as before, but at night, there was a particularly pungent and offensive odor unique to cowsheds.

Every day, he faced the harsh morning wind and trod on the damp frost, going with the master to the vast fields or climbing the steep firewood mountain, until darkness swallowed the earth. Except for lunchtime, there was no rest at all. And at night, by the light of a soybean-sized kerosene lamp, he husked several pecks of rice alone or accompanied the mistress to grind a peck of wheat, which was also a common occurrence.

In order to stimulate the remaining strength in his large frame, in order to make him completely forget fatigue and rest, the master constantly injected stimulants. The so-called stimulants were nothing more than "So-and-so's daughter is beautiful and talented. As long as you work hard for me, I will definitely arrange for you to marry her," or "I've told you, her father is about to agree." With this kind of empty talk that never materialized, the simpleton constantly and wholeheartedly sold his only possession - his labor.

When he was working in the fields or chopping firewood in the mountains, he always hummed vulgar and lewd mountain songs. The singing was rough and loud, causing the surrounding high mountains and deep valleys to echo powerfully.

When he was tired of singing, his voice gradually became weaker. But he wasn't silent. Replacing the loud singing was a low-pitched soliloquy. He chatted incoherently, sometimes seeming to talk about his hometown, the local bullies, and his own life and wife.

"So beautiful! Dragon and phoenix eyes, receding chin, three-inch feet. So beautiful!" These were the words he always used to describe his wife.

His tangled conversation, the conversation containing endless suffering and sorrow, the fire-like glint of anger in the depths of his eyes, the small, crystal-clear tears floating in the corners of his eyes, and the bitter face containing a strong smile like a razor blade, all showed people a heartbreaking history of a trampled farmer, and the helpless sorrow of wanting to tear up this heartbreaking history but being unable to.

"So where is your wife now?" someone asked.

"Someone else took her."

"Who?"

"Zhang Xingshan."

Then he raised his hoarse voice and sang, his singing somewhat trembling:

"Zhang Xingshan, not a human being, seizing another man's wife is a serious crime!"

"Why?"

"Three stone and five rent grains."

"You couldn't pay three stone and five rent grains, so they took your wife? These years have been famine years!"

Page 21

Shanghai Newspaper Supplement Movie Special

The Banning of Co-Starring Films for Men and Women Amid the Retro Movement (Part 2)

— Danfeng

For example, if the elegant and charming demeanor of people's concubines were to be put on the silver screen as newsreels, there would have to be disguised grooms and guards shouting and following her, and these grooms and guards would be men. What would happen in this case? Of course, this is malicious propaganda that should be banned. But if a certain film company were to make a film promoting highway construction, which is a great and remarkable work for the Party and the country, then there would inevitably be some ladies or daughters dressed neatly to throw champagne or cut ribbons. At the same time, there would be no shortage of committee comrades giving speeches and helping out, making a lively scene and embellishing the occasion. In this case, there would again be men and women mingling together, which is greatly inconsistent with the ancient customs of the Three Dynasties. What would happen in this case?

The situation with domestic films is like this, but on the other hand, what about foreign films? Everyone knows that foreign films have embraces, kisses, "I love you," and "I want you." The mutual attraction between men and women is quite embarrassing. Compared to Chinese films, they are much more nauseating. Confucius would shake his head upon seeing them, and even Liu Xiahui would inevitably be confused. Their distance from the moral concepts of adults and gentlemen is a clearly obvious fact. So, shouldn't they all be banned? Needless to say, "When the Great Way prevails, all under heaven will work for the common good." According to what the "Bible" shows, of course, we must treat China and foreign countries as one and the same. However, if this is really the case, I'm afraid it won't be easy to do. Because if we do this, wouldn't we be harming the goodwill of friendly nations? Wouldn't we be offending the foreign masters? This is definitely not a fun thing to do.

Let's talk about women. In Japan, before the Meiji Restoration, they were not allowed to eat at the same table as their husbands. When men ate, women knelt beside them to serve them rice until they were finished eating, and then they could eat. This cruel rule may still exist in some rural areas of Japan today. So, if China does the same, is it preparing to be a subjugated nation? Of course, we dare not speculate on the profound wisdom of adults and gentlemen.

Soon, some people predict that in the future, Guangzhou will build a high wall in the middle of the road to separate men and women. According to this example, future Chinese films will definitely only allow men to ride horses and shoot, or only allow women to embrace and dance. When necessary, talk about homosexual love? Otherwise, only "Lone Army Souls" or "Feminine" will be allowed to be screened in China. However, there are too few of these films, and it is indeed not easy to do.

However, we remember that "Qiongdong Storm" or "A Trouble Within the Fold," which were produced under the command of generals, both depicted the shameless behavior of men and women who were attracted to each other. I wonder if they are also on the list of banned films? Otherwise, wouldn't it be a bit painful to get a red face from slapping oneself? (The End)

Film Reviews

Review of "Little Miss Marker"

— Ling He

Little Miss Marker

丨丨Grand Theater丨丨

Under a kind of conscience and morality, the playwright attempts to use the method of persuading with good words to influence the general unemployed ruffians in his works. This motive makes the film somewhat bear the mission of education. In any case, his intention is commendable.

However, we must move people with truth, that is to say, if it is not 100% true, it will not generate the power to move people. From this point of view, the playwright of "Little Miss Marker" has not done it. He departs from economic conditions and teaches with empty words.

We shouldn't completely believe that those gamblers and the like can sacrifice everything for the sake of a little girl, right? We also wouldn't believe that they could hold a grand masquerade ball to win the girl's heart, right? Things like this really make us believe that it's just the playwright talking.

Regarding this aspect, we completely disagree with the views of soft theorists. They believe that what is expressed in the film does not necessarily have to be something that really exists in the world. Our requirement, however, is to express a truth that is more true than reality from the common and ordinary lives of ordinary people. The shortcoming of "Little Miss Marker" lies here. If the playwright is not too exaggerated in his fantasy, then we believe that it can make people cry with gratitude to depict it in terms of "human love."

Because of the content's decision, the director ultimately has no way to hide the flaws in the script. His strength is only in creating a very bright atmosphere, allowing the plot to progress without any stagnation. This major achievement is due to the child, a natural outpouring of goodness and beauty, like a myth, also like a fable, filling the screen with joyful humor. Although we feel unrealistic exaggeration in a few scenes, in some scenes, that kind of goodness and beauty, overflowing in a static atmosphere, is indeed something that vulgar directors cannot do. These are particularly evident in scenes such as the child telling stories before going to sleep or innocent prayers. From the moment the child is kicked by a horse, the climax of the play is formed until Stevie donates blood. The anxious movements of everyone, as well as Stevie seeing the serious expressions on people's faces from outside the door, and the atmosphere during the surgery, all show that the director has a very good grasp of capturing the audience's sympathy.

As mentioned earlier, the main achievement of this play is that the young actress Shirley Temple has achieved great success. Almost every word and every action of hers, because she is easy to be loved, for most of the time, she is teaching people to laugh with joy. Secondly, Adolphe Menjou should be considered the most successful. Compared to his previous plays, which are known for their suave and unrestrained style, we believe that he has achieved a unique style in this play. The deceased Dorothy Dell also performed well, and the rest were just average.

Mae West Isn't Leaving Yet

— Fu

You can all guess how much longer that hourglass-figured woman, Mae West, can hold out on the screen, but Mae West herself is not worried about herself. She has heard all the speculation and criticism about her from the outside world. Some people say that she has acted in three films in a row, but only the first one was successful. Therefore, she can only act in one or two more films at most, and then she can retire to her hometown. But she is very confident in herself. She says that the reason she was able to become a star as soon as she appeared on the screen is entirely because she is a "mature artist," and not an accidental success. She may hit the bullseye with one shot, or she may fail completely, but once she has hit the bullseye, can't she maintain it? Therefore, she feels that there is no reason for people to say that she will not be able to stand in Hollywood for long. But she has now decided to be very careful about the films she will act in in the future and the number of films she will act in. Of course, Mae West is an exceptionally intelligent woman, and she must have her own wonderful methods to maintain her position.

"Smart Guy Meets Smart Guy" posture of the duel between Nancy and Maurice, screened at the Jishi Theater.

Dorothy Dell Has Passed Away

— Bo'er

"Death always comes in threes. Lilinda Xumen and Liu Jiadai are already two. I wonder who the third one is?" I vaguely remember that not long ago, Dorothy was talking to people in the company. At that time, someone said to her, "Wouldn't that be you?" "Now it has come true. The two things happened only twelve hours apart.

After finishing things in the company, she wanted to rush back to attend a banquet. Unfortunately, on the road, the driver lost control. The car first hit a large rock, and then hit a wooden telephone pole, rolling for about 100 yards before being completely shattered. Dorothy was seriously injured and died on the spot. The driver also died six hours later after being taken to the hospital. He was Dr. Carl Wagner.

Dorothy was a rising star who was recently discovered. She usually joked with people, saying that she would either drown or die in a car accident. Now her prophecy has come true. She was a talented actress. Recently, her reputation was no less than that of Claudette Colbert. The most heartbroken by her death was five-year-old Shirley Temple, because she became very close after collaborating on "Little Miss Marker." Alas! Heaven always refuses to let talented people live long!

Silver Miscellaneous Talks

— Bai Pin

Stars often have disputes over listing issues, thinking that their name being listed later is a great humiliation!

In fact, this mentality is the opposite of the audience's mentality. If a certain star occupies a very important position, even taking the lead, then the audience should pay special attention to that star. If the results are good, it is acceptable. Otherwise, paying attention with great hope, but the result is disappointing, so-called "The greater the hope, the greater the disappointment." Then, although a certain star occupies an advantage in the listing, if the results are not good, then although "obtained" it is not enough to compensate for the "loss"!

The Film Novel "Woman" Is a Bestseller

The film novel "Woman," published by the Times Publishing Company, has been selling very well since its publication. It is said that the book has a correct consciousness, a fluent writing style, and is accompanied by more than a dozen valuable illustrations in addition to the text. It is printed on exquisite copperplate paper, clear and beautiful. It is also said that when the film is screened in famous theaters, it is sold on-site to increase audience interest. There are not many books left, so those who want to buy them should hurry up. Each copy is 40 cents, and all bookstores in various cities are selling them.

Film Novel

Good Son and Good Wife (Born to be Kissed) (13)

— Xin Zhi

Tom, after hearing his father and Eddie argue, felt that Eddie had not been honest or complete in what she had told him before. So, he angrily said to Eddie, "You're lying to me... About Chris Kins' infidelity... and that man last night, how long have you two been together?" At this point, Eddie could no longer stand it. She cried and screamed, "Get out of here!" Tom, when she screamed, didn't move. So, Eddie screamed again, "Get out of here!" Pan Qi took a step and went out. He turned around and softly shouted to Tom, "Son, let's go." Tom had no choice but to follow his father out. Eddie was left alone, shouting behind Tom, "Tom! Tom! Come back! I don't want you to go!" But he didn't know if Tom heard her, or if he heard her, he ignored her. No understanding. No forgiveness. No sound of footsteps returning. Eddie was alone, her heart filled with sorrow and worry. In this sorrow and worry, she made a decision... She would never talk about love again... She would no longer be a good woman... She must take revenge... Pan Qi must receive due punishment!

Since Tom followed his father out of Jefferson Lai City Prison, he could not quickly forget Eddie. Later, his father persuaded him to go to London with him. Although he agreed without much thought, when the day came when they boarded the ship and were about to set sail, Tom suddenly told his father, "Father, I still need to go ashore once. I forgot something." His father was about to ask him what it was when he ran away, running from the gangplank straight to the shore. He ran to the shore, hailed a taxi, and handed a slip of paper to the driver. The driver took it and looked at it. Written on it were the words "Jefferson Lai City Prison." He looked at Tom with some surprise, and then drove the car away. At the same time, another car came and stopped at the pier. The door opened, and the one who ran out was Chuli, who was there to see them off. He came out and looked back at one of the two women in the carriage. She was dressed luxuriously, wearing an expensive mink coat, but she looked unhappy. Chuli said to the woman, "Eddie, my beautiful, you can wait for me in the car. I'll be down in a moment." She looked at the other woman and said, "Jidi, you accompany her." He patted Eddie's thigh, as if Eddie was already his person, and said, "From here, I'm going to take you home."

Eddie silently watched him walk away, not saying a word, as if she had a plan in mind. She... would go home with him... What else mattered now? Suddenly, she felt a flash before her eyes. She saw the person who had taken photos of her and the unknown man in her room that night. She suddenly jumped out of the car. She chased after him and grabbed his arm. She whispered to him eagerly. The person smiled. She went on the ship with him from the gangplank. At this time, Pan was talking with ordinary people, as well as many reporters, and friends who had come to say goodbye to him. The photographer walked in front of him and said, "Mr. Pan Qi, let me take a picture of you, okay!" Pan Qi nodded happily. The photographer also said, "Please stand a little to the left." Pan Qi also agreed! He stood in the place he pointed to, which was right in front of the door of his private room. Then the photographer shouted loudly, "Okay, Mr. Pan Qi!" He didn't seem to need to shout so loudly. No sooner said than done, when he shouted, the door of Pan Qi's bedroom opened! A person jumped out from inside! (To be continued)
